But these made her ass look fantastic – at least according to Jen. She’d been there when Agatha bought them, when they’d gone to lunch with Naomi and she’d enticed them into taking a longer lunch break to check out some new chic store that catered mainly to teens and college kids. 

“Let’s be young again!” Naomi had said, tugging on a pair of heart-shaped sunglasses. “We can play dress-up!”

Jen had rolled her eyes, but she’d done so affectionately, grinning sideways at Agatha as they started checking out the selection of over-priced jeans. Agatha had picked out a pair that she would probably have never actually bought had Jen not let out a low whistle and told her that she didn’t realize Agatha could actually have definition in your backside, Harkness .

Naomi had swatted her for that comment, but all three of them laughed as Agatha put them back.

Two months later, Naomi had gifted the jeans to her for Christmas.

Three years later, Agatha tugged them from her dresser, tags and all, and tried them on. They were slightly looser than they’d been in the store. But still tighter than anything she normally wore.

And her ass still looked fantastic in them.

Still, Agatha paired them with a simple purple blouse that was made of a papery material and a comfy cardigan that she could get away with wearing in lieu of a jacket on the cool Autumn night. 

Jen’s off-shoulder dress was definitely too cool for the weather, but she didn’t let it bother her. Agatha predicted she would have already stolen the cardigan right off Agatha’s back if it did, anyhow.

The bar was warm as they stepped inside, and there were flags hanging up all over the place. Most were pride flags, but there were some national flags, as well.

“When do you think is the right time to come out as Irish?” Jen whispered in Agatha’s ear, making her snort as they made their way to the back of the bar, where a stage had been set up with several rows of folding chairs and a few tables. The first row was all chairs, set just three feet from the edge of the stage. Most of the row had been filled save for three spots.

Agatha immediately spotted Alice’s head of black hair and fiery orange streaks. She glanced up at Jen, who was giving Alice a goofy grin already. She was smitten .

“Aww,” Agatha teased, under her breath. “Someone’s in lo-ove .” She nudged Jen in the side again.

Jen responded by flicking her ear. “Shut the fuck up,” she huffed, but it was hard to keep that grin off her face for too long. Especially when Alice turned and spotted them, waving them both over as she stood. “Ohmygod, Agatha,” Jen gasped, “she’s wearing a bow tie. She’s so cute.” She placed one hand over her heart as they approached a woman standing at the back of the crowd.

“Tickets?” she asked them.

“Our names should be on the list,” Agatha said. “Agatha Harkness and Jennifer Kale.”

“Ah,” the woman smiled, “friends of Rio. Very good. Do you have your IDs?”

Agatha and Jen fished their IDs out – Jen from her purse and Agatha from her very tight pocket. They handed them over and the woman checked them, humming and nodding. 

“Fantastic,” she said, holding up a stamp. “Let me see your left hands, please.”

They each held out their left hand for a stamp.

Agatha snorted at the sight of a ‘crone’ (appropriately labeled as such) next to the words ‘Over 21’ on her hand.

“You guys allow people under 21 in this bar after dark?” she asked, raising one brow.

“This bar is eighteen and older,” the woman informed her. “Under 21’s get the designation of ‘Maiden’ when applicable. You can’t order a drink without getting carded and stamped.”

“Did we even need tickets for the show?” Jen asked. “Couldn’t we have sat at the bar and watched?”

“I mean, sure,” the woman said, “but not many people who are actually interested in the show prefer to sit there. The sound gets a little wonky the further you are from the stage. We have, like, one speaker in this entire place hooked up to Rio’s mic. And it’s behind her. Best way to catch the jokes is by sitting in the audience, which is full tonight, by the way.”

“Wow,” Agatha said, her eyes widening a little. “She must bring in a lot of business.”

“Oh, you have no idea,” the woman said. “She’s hilarious. Best decision Tony ever made was giving her a regular gig.”

“Tony?” Agatha asked.

“The owner.” The woman nodded in the direction of the bar, where a man with a pair of shades and a goatee was wiping down a glass while laughing with a few patrons. “His daughter, Morgan, came out a few years ago and he opened this place for her. It’s technically not a lesbian bar, but she’s gonna be the owner someday, so he decided to market it as a queer safe space. Great guy.”

“That’s so sweet,” Jen said, placing her hand over her heart. 

“Yeah,” Agatha said, looking over her shoulder at the guy again. He watched as a teen girl with braces and bright eyes stepped up next to him, hugging him around the waist as he laughed and pressed his lips to the top of her head. She looked at him like he hung the moon and he looked down at her like she was his whole world.

Agatha wondered if her father ever looked at her like that. She knew her mother never did.

“Come on, Ags,” Jen urged, taking her by the arm. “The show is gonna start soon.”

“You don’t want a drink?” Agatha asked, blinking rapidly before turning to Jen.

“We have waitresses for the show,” the usher informed them. “Just flag one of them down and they’ll bring you anything you want. Rio said everything’s on her tab tonight.”

“Typical,” Agatha huffed. “I literally told her I’d be the one buying tonight.”

“Ooh,” Jen said, “then I’ll take a–”

“For her ,” Agatha huffed, tugging her down the aisle to the front row. “You have your own date to buy you drinks.”

“So this is a date for you and Rio,” Jen teased under her breath, a little bit gloaty.

“No, it’s not–”

“Hey, Alice!” Jen cooed, ignoring Agatha (but keeping that infuriating smirk on her face) as she wriggled out of her grasp and reached out to hug the shorter woman. 

Alice really did look kind of cute in her bowtie, Agatha had to admit. She was also wearing a short-sleeve, collared navy blue shirt that complemented the burnt umber shade of the bowtie around her neck. Her hair was half-up in a messy bun on the back of her head, and her eyes were lined thickly in black eyeliner. Agatha doubted she was wearing much other makeup, but she looked nice, nonetheless.

And nervous. She looked very, very nervous – like a little kid on picture day trying very hard not to ruin the clothes their mother had hand-picked and ironed for them.

It was adorable.

“Hi, Jen,” Alice said, mooning up at her. Agatha saw the slight shake in her hands even as Alice tried to hide them. “Hi, Agatha.”

“Hey, Alice,” Agatha said, poking her head around Jen’s freakishly tall body. 

“You look so good,” Jen said, stroking the bowtie. Agatha could practically see Alie’s tail begin to wag as her entire body perked up, her cheeks going as pink as Jen’s dress.

“Thanks!” she said. “You too!” 

Jen giggled – giggled like a schoolgirl – and took Alice’s hand, the two of them claiming the seats on the aisle and forcing Agatha to shimmy past them to the center-most seats. There was still one left. 

Dulce’s seat .

Agatha was a bit nervous about seeing the younger artist again, especially having the knowledge she did now. Did Dulce have that same knowledge? Did she know that Agatha had won the silent auction on her photograph? Did Rio ?

Agatha’s head was swimming with questions as she took her seat next to Jen in the first row.

“Miss Harkness?” a tentative voice greeted. Agatha jumped a little bit, turning just as Dulce approached, looking very shy and so very young.

Rio was right: it was the dimples that made her look younger.

Even with that crone stamped on her hand, she looked like a child.

A child that Rio had apparently raised when she was still a child herself.

Oh, this was getting so complicated.

Agatha forced a smile as she stood and reached out, pulling Dulce into a hug. “Hello, Dulce,” she said, warmly, obviously shocking the girl by the way she stiffened in Agatha’s arms. “How are you, dear?” 

“I’m okay,” Dulce said, relaxing slightly after a moment. She pulled back with a slightly more open smile, glancing between Agatha and Jen, who greeted her from behind Agatha. “Hi, Miss Kale,” she said.

“Ugh,” Jen said, “as if we’re her kindergarten teachers. Call me Jen , sweetie. And this is Agatha . We’re all in our twenties.” She reached around Agatha to press air kisses to Dulce’s cheeks before sitting back down with Alice, who probably gave her a little wave or nod or something else that Agatha didn’t see because she was still facing Dulce.

“So,” Dulce said, also taking her seat as Agatha mirrored her, “how, exactly, do you two know Alice and my sister?”

Agatha’s eyes widened at that. Rio hadn’t told her? Why?

“Um,” Agatha said, glancing back at Jen and Alice. Jen was giving her a questioning look like even she wasn’t quite sure what to say. Alice echoed the look, tilting her head slightly at Agatha. “It’s kind of a long story…”

Just at that moment, the lights started to dim around them, signaling the beginning of the show.

“Ladies and gentlemen,” a voice said from behind the curtain, “please take your seats now and finish placing your drink orders. If you need a drink during the show, please don’t get up. Just flag down one of our servers and they’ll get it for you. You won’t want to miss Westview’s very own “Sit-Down” Comedian, Rio Vidal . Put your hands together for Miss Rio Vidal, everybody!”

Agatha and Dulce simultaneously turned toward the stage just as the curtains parted, revealing Rio on her stool, adjusting her mic. Agatha’s throat went dry at the sight of her, her cheeks going pink and hot.

She hoped the rapidly dimming lights on the audience and the brightening lights on the stage hid it well enough. The applause around them seemed to cover the sound of her heart pounding in her chest well enough.

Still, Rio’s gaze snagged on hers almost immediately, and she gave Agatha a coy, lopsided grin as she leaned forward to start talking into the mic.

“Hey,” she said, her voice warm and sweet as honey. It felt, momentarily, like they were the only two people in the room, energy crackling between them, enough to power a small nation, before her gaze shifted to the audience behind Agatha. “How’s everybody doing tonight?” Rio asked, her smile widening as her voice got louder. 

There were cheers in response.

“So, just okay, then?” Rio asked. “I said , ‘HOW IS EVERYBODY DOING TONIGHT?’!” 

The cheers got louder around them. Even people at the bar behind them were cheering.

“That’s more like it!” Rio said. “Hi, all! Thanks so much for coming out here tonight. My name is Rio, as most of you know, because most of you are alcoholics and were here anyway.” Some laughter throughout the crowd. “Nah, I’m just kidding. You’re not all alcoholics. Some of you are lesbians.”

More cheers scattered throughout the crowd. Agatha laughed.

“There’s definitely a lot of overlap there, too,” Rio said. “Don’t be modest. Just make sure you tip your waitresses. They gotta make a living around here, too.” The waitresses cheered. “I gotchu,” Rio said, blowing a kiss to the servers. 

Agatha felt a frisson of what could vaguely be described as jealousy (though she would never admit it) run down her spine.

“Anyway, there are quite a few familiar faces here tonight. I love to see that. Thank you for paying my tab tonight, guys, I really appreciate it.” More laughter. Rio beamed, flashing that gap between her teeth. “Okay, so let’s get to the jokes, then.” 

Agatha cheered with the rest of the crowd.

Rio winked at her.

 

Rio’s pulse pounded in her neck as the curtains opened, but there was a sense of calm that came over her every time she saw the familiar faces of her audience each week. 

She knew most of the people in the crowd. They were bar regulars. They ran tabs as they laughed uproariously at her jokes. They clapped the loudest sometimes. Some of them could get obnoxious, but there were never any serious incidents in the few years since she’d started performing.

And then there was Alice, who had been showing up to as many show nights as she could manage since they met at group therapy. She’d been there for Rio pretty much since that first meeting, which…well, Rio had never really had a best friend before.

Sure, she’d had friends. She’d had friends in school. She was a funny, nice, smart, and somewhat sociable person. But when Dulce was born, she’d become a caretaker, which didn’t allow for much of a social life when her parents were expecting her to share in – and then take over – parental duties whenever she was home. She couldn’t really have playdates when she was expected to feed or change a baby. Her parents rarely allowed her to go over to other kids’ homes because they might need her help with something.

In high school, it got easier to socialize because Dulce was also getting older and easier to handle. She was a good kid and could be distracted with a snack and some crayons and paper when Rio needed her to be. But nobody in her life was ever her best friend. 

Not like Alice.

Except for Dulce. She could definitively say that, despite their difficult and definitely damaging childhood, Dulce was her very best friend. A best friend who showered her with love and affection and gifts on both Mother’s and Father’s Day, mind you. 

Rio’s mother had been upset by this the first time it happened, when Dulce had bypassed her the morning of Mother’s Day and brought her handmade card straight to Rio at the breakfast table instead of to her. She was six and had learned that her biggest support wasn’t the woman who’d given birth to her, but rather the one who had raised her and never once complained. 

Dulce was unapologetic about it, too, which Rio had tried not to laugh (or cry) about when she’d opened the card, which had a dead daisy in it (one that Dulce had picked herself during recess the previous week) and found a picture of herself and Dulce holding hands.

(She still had that card, somewhere.)

Their dad was less concerned when Dulce pulled the same stunt on Father’s Day and Rio received a drawing of herself standing at a grill (pretty impressively drawn even for an artistic six-year-old) and holding a basketball on her hip.

(She still had that one, too.)

Rio always figured she could have resented having to take care of Dulce as an adolescent, being forced to raise her while her parents were able to live their lives pretending to be childless adults eight percent of the time (generously) and only coming around when they wanted to do something fun with the daughters they seemed to only remember existed on occasion. 

But what good would that have done? What good would it have done her to be angry all the time at somebody who didn’t choose to be born, let alone to be born to two irresponsible and selfish assholes? Dulce needed support and love, and Rio, despite everything her parents put her through, was able and willing to give it to her.

And she’d do it all over again without hesitation.

Rio did a few warm up jokes about the length of time she’d been doing her “sit down” comedy at Westview, which morphed into her talking about her leg.

“I don’t like to call it my bad leg ,” she said, getting up from her stool as she pulled the mic from the stand and waited for the feeling to fully reach her toes before she took a few steps across the stage. “Bad implies that it’s doing this on purpose, which I don’t fully believe.” She got a few chuckles for that as she hobbled. “It’s not like my leg chooses when to work perfectly; it’s like this all the time. Not like I’m going to wake up one day in the middle of the field because it decided to go for a run without my knowledge.” The crowd laughed and Rio grinned. “My god, could you imagine? Having a leg that decides when it works right. Like those people who pretend to be bad at chores so they don’t have to do them? What losers, amiright…ladies?” There were some cheers from the audience, mostly female. “Yeah, I know the kinda shit some of y’all go through with the men in your lives. You have my deepest condolences, but I’ve literally never been so happy to be a lesbian in my life.” Even louder cheers, some from the very same women. “I mean, not that women can’t also play that…what’s it called?”

“Weaponized incompetence!” a few people shouted from the audience.

“Yes, that!” Rio laughed. “We’ve got some victims here tonight. My condolences, ladies. You deserve better.”

“Yeah, I do!” one voice replied.

“Tell him!” Rio said, with a snap.

“It’s my wife !” the person said.

“Ooh! You see?!” Rio said, grinning at the rest of the audience as she knocked her cane on the ground. “Lesbians can be incompetent, too! Girl power!” She snapped while the audience laughed. “We truly can be anything we set our mind to.” She perched herself femininely on her stool, giving the crowd a pouty face before dissolving into laughter. “Seriously, though, why do people do that? You put more energy into pretending you can’t do something than actually just doing the thing. And all you’re doing is annoying the other person in your relationship. That can not turn out well for at least some of you. Has nobody ever seen Snapped ?”

That got her a few laughs, but not enough in her opinion.

“Ooh, there are some people here who don’t know what that show’s about and it shows. Go home and watch it. And start loading the dishwasher correctly , Jerry .” She gave a playful glare to the audience. “Or Mary.” She shrugged. “Just do what you’re supposed to do to make your spouse’s and your life easier.”

She got cheers and applause for that and Rio let it soak in for a moment, taking a deep breath.

Then

“Who here likes tits?”

Several hands went up. There were cheers.

“Oh my god!” Rio gushed, placing a hand on her chest. “Me, too!” She snorted to herself as people laughed. “ Actually , I saw a couple of Great Tits just yesterday here in town.” She glanced down to Agatha, who was already pressing her lips together to suppress her laughter. “I saw some boobies, too. And a couple of incredible hooters. I mean, they are just so beautiful, you know?” She sighed dreamily, looking off into the distance for a moment. “And can you believe I didn’t even have to go to some club to see them? They were just right out in the open for me to gawk at, in the middle of an art gallery, no less! Right here, in Westview!” There were some gasps throughout the audience and Rio grinned.

Perfect .

She feigned confusion. “What?” she said. “You guys have never seen a pair of nice tits in an art gallery? Uncultured. Art galleries are a fine place to showcase great tits and boobies and hooters . Don’t act all scandalized now when you were just cheering for them not ten seconds ago! The Craft uptown has a whole installation centered around a pair of great tits.” More murmurs and gasps. “Oh ye Puritans,” Rio laughed. “You see them all the time out in the wild, don’t you? They’re all over the place in this country. You see them in books, on TV, in magazines…hell, I’ve seen them in the park a time or two.” 

Dead silence.

Except Agatha, who looked like she was about to do her little snorty laugh. Rio wanted to bask in that moment just before she completely broke. She took a beat. 

Then two.

“What do you people have against birds?” she demanded playfully.

The silence broke with a murmur of confusion from most in the crowd. Those who understood immediately began to laugh. 

Including Agatha, whose snorts echoed despite her attempts to smother them. Rio couldn’t fight her responding laughter as she attempted to continue with the joke, putting on a faux scandalized look.

“Wait a second,” she said, eyeing the crowd with the caution of a church lady clutching her pearls. “Wait a gosh-darn second! Did you all think I was talking about…” she leaned in to whisper into the mic, “ breasts ?” Murmurs of affirmation, confirmation, and confusion were her reply and she let out a dramatic gasp. “How dare you! I am a fucking lady!” She turned up her nose, but she couldn’t keep herself from peeking out at Agatha, who was in hysterics while Alice and Dulce stared at her, wide-eyed and confused. 

Jen, obviously, knew exactly what Rio was referencing, but she seemed more entertained by Agatha’s red face and snorty laughs as she fought to contain herself.

Rio’s heart did a stupid little flip in her chest at the sights and sounds of Agatha Harkness absolutely losing her shit. Damn, she was cute.

But then her eyes shifted to the left, where Dulce was sitting, staring at her in that unblinking way she sometimes stared. It unnerved Rio every single time.

Tonight was no different.

Especially since this time she looked…angry.

Shit .

Rio grimaced internally as she moved on with her set, ignoring her sister’s piercing stares that followed her throughout the rest of her show.

Chapter 10: Dealbreakers

Chapter Summary

Rio and Dulce have a hard discussion and things are explained. Then Dulce officially meets her heroes. Then there's pizza and controversy, yum. And then there's...a little more. Enjoy!

Chapter Notes

It's 2am here in New York.

I have a doctor's appointment at 9am.

Help 🙂

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Ten

Dulce Vidal didn’t have many adults she could look up to in her childhood.

She didn’t have aunts or uncles. She didn’t have grandparents. Her parents’ friends typically only came around after she’d already been tucked in for the night (by Rio, of course), so she didn’t really get to know any of them well enough to have reasonable role models. 

Not that she thought a bunch of childless adults who acted closer to somebody her age were what one might think when the phrase ‘role model’ was being used. 

Rio tried to give her other role models to look up to: scientists, like Einstein and Curie; artists, like Van Gogh and O’Keefe and Rembrandt; and successful businesswomen, like Oprah and Kiran Mazumdar-Shaw. She also introduced Dulce to different genres of music, books, and movies. They vegged out on the couch on weekends to watch old black and white films, and Dulce cuddled up to Rio’s side while she read aloud from picture books, then later helped Dulce learn to read using those same books.

She put on Selena songs while they cooked dinner, dancing around the kitchen as they giggled and sang in Spanish, which Rio taught Dulce all by herself since her parents didn’t seem to have much of an interest in their children outside the odd day when her mother remembered she had them.

Their father barely acknowledged their existence even when he was around.

Dulce didn’t have many adults in her life to look up to, but she at least had Rio.

And Rio agreed never to keep things from her – not if she could help it.

So why had she kept this from her?

Agatha Harkness was sitting next to her right now, trying desperately to suppress her snorts with her hands as Rio told some joke about seeing Great Tits at Agatha Harkness’s art gallery. 

Agatha Harkness, who was one of the successful women that Dulce actually looked up to. One she had the luck to live in the same town as. One that Rio knew she loved (in a purely aspirational sense, of course) because Agatha wasn’t much older than herself and already had a successful career as not only an artist but as a gallery owner, as well. 

Agatha Harkness was practically Dulce’s Taylor Swift .

So why did Rio never mention the fact that, apparently, the two of them were friends.

She stared at her sister, unblinkingly, for the entirety of her set. She didn’t take out her phone to film like she normally would have. She just stared. She knew that it unnerved Rio when she did this, but, in her defense, she only did it when she was very, very mad.

And that was very much an understatement right now.

Until the joke about the tits and the boobies and the hooters (oh my!), Dulce was willing to believe that it was Alice who had formally introduced them after somehow meeting her date (Jennifer fucking Kale , who was also a big deal in the suburban New Jersey art world, by the way) in the wild, but that wouldn’t explain why Rio had gone to the art gallery without her . 

Rio wasn’t even that into art. It was Dulce who’d dragged her through the exhibits, cooing over compositions and geeking out over light exposure. Rio liked some of the pieces well enough to spend money on prints and creative keychains in the gift shop, but she didn’t typically peruse the art gallery by herself . Dulce was always with her for that.

Well, at least Dulce had thought that. Until now.

She narrowed her eyes as she caught Rio’s gaze and didn’t miss the thick swallowing motion as Rio quickly averted it, standing once more to pace the stage as she continued her set, moving on from the art gallery to something about the park and nature and whatever-the-fuck. People were still laughing, but Dulce didn’t find this funny anymore.

How the fuck did they meet?

Westview was a small town, this was true. It’s possible that Rio had met Agatha somewhere mundane, like the cafe or the park or–

Dulce’s eyes widened. The park . 

The cute runner in the park was Agatha freaking Harkness! It had to be!

But then why would Rio keep that from her? Did she think Dulce was going to start stalking her or something?!?! She wasn’t that obsessed!

…

Okay, no, Dulce probably would have spent more time in the park just to get a glimpse of Agatha Harkness and possibly become her best friend and potential future business partner – but that was just networking! It was smart ! Rio understood that.

Didn’t she?

Rio had never given Dulce a reason not to trust her. In fact, she’d given Dulce about a million reasons to trust her over anybody else. It would have taken a major betrayal to get Dulce even halfway on somebody else’s side over her own sister’s. Even then, she didn’t think she could really hold a grudge against the woman who literally changed her diapers when she was just starting adolescence. She wasn’t like a typical teen parent in which she actively chose to be dumb and have unprotected sex – Rio didn’t birth Dulce! She didn’t really need to raise her like she did.

That alone earned her, at least in Dulce’s eyes, the benefit of the doubt.

She just couldn’t figure out why, then, Rio had kept something so big from her. She knew that Rio would find a way to explain it. She believed that Rio would tell her the truth about it, too. Wouldn’t she?

Something rumbled in her chest at the thought. Something uncomfortable. Something like doubt .

She did not like it.

 

Rio’s set ended, like many do, with a standing ovation.

“Wow,” she said, still perched on her stool, her leg feeling staticky and useless, “that’s so rude of you all, thank you.” There was laughter along with harder applause. Rio laughed with them and waved, forcing herself to her feet. “Thank you all so much for coming!” she said. “Remember to tip your waitresses and close out your tabs. Or don’t! Stay for a while and help fund Morgan Stark’s college education! See you next time!” She blew a kiss as the curtains closed on her. 

As soon as she was no longer in the spotlight, her entire body slumped back onto the stool in exhaustion.

She had stood up too many times for somebody who called herself the ‘sit-down’ comedian. But Dulce’s stare had really gotten into her head. Every time she looked over at the kid, she seemed to be staring into her very soul , her eyes narrowing minutely every single time. It was just as unnerving as when she was little, looking like the girl from The Ring with her long black hair and pale skin (Dulce was not an outdoor child). 

Rio felt, several times, like jumping off the stage and kneeling at her feet, like explaining to her what had happened, how she and Alice had met Agatha and Jen, and why she’d been unable to tell her about it. But she’d been trapped onstage, doing the same show she’d done for…

God , she didn’t even really know when she’d started doing this show now. It must have been at least three years. Tony had bought the place for Morgan and she was about to be nineteen, just starting her freshman year of college while still living at home.

She came out as a teenager, a young one. Was she fourteen or fifteen when she first came out?

Rio shook her head. What the fuck did that matter right now? Point is, Rio couldn’t have disrupted the show to grovel at her sister’s feet because that shit wasn’t funny! She had destroyed her sister’s trust! She doubted that she’d be able to regain it back even if she could tell Dulce the truth right now.

She groaned, rubbing her face with her hands. 

“Okay,” a voice said, making Rio yelp, “explain.”

“ Jesus Christ! ” Rio exclaimed, fighting to stay on the stool. Dulce was standing there, shadowed by the mellow lighting of the stage now that there were no spotlights on them. “You need a bell around your neck,” she huffed. “You’ve been spending too much time with Reaper.” Their cat liked to creep around and attack their ankles like she was hunting them. It was part of the reason she often wore a bell on her collar, though she was adept at slipping out of it, so she could play her little stalking game.

Swan’s steps were too heavy to stalk prey. She preferred to wail at her food bowl for her meat like the mustachioed princess she was.

“Don’t deflect,” Dulce said, her voice firm. “Explain.”

“Explain what, exactly?” Rio asked, grimacing even as the question escaped her lips. She was nearly a full half-foot taller than her sister, even sitting on the stool, but Rio found her shoulders hunching as Dulce took a step closer to her, that look in her unblinking eyes intensifying. “Okay, okay,” she squeaked, holding her hands up in surrender. “What do you want to know?”

“How did you two meet ?” Dulce demanded, folding her arms over her chest. “Let’s start there.”

“We…can’t start there, actually,” Rio said, practically a turtle with how far her head was in between her shoulders. “Not without Agatha.”

“What?” Dulce asked, furrowing her brow.

“It will make sense,” Rio promised. “Eventually. But why are we wasting time here when we could be out there , talking to your heroes?”

Dulce scoffed. “They’re not my heroes,” she huffed, but she was blushing.

“Don’t lie,” Rio teased, standing up and placing one hand on her sister’s back, ushering her out while her cane kept her steady in the other hand. “I’ve seen the newspaper clippings in your bedroom.”

“ What?! ” Dulce practically choked as Rio led her down the steps and out the side door into the audience. 

Alice, Jen, and Agatha were standing there with a handful of others who wanted Rio’s autograph. It happened at a few shows every now and then since Dulce was regularly posting her on TikTok. Some fans from out of town would find where she does her shows (they never posted their location since they didn’t want the bar to become overrun with lesbian fangirls) and come out in support. 

Luckily, these fans never shared the name and location of the bar, either. Rio knew that couldn’t really last.

“Hey, there,” she said, grinning at a handful of twenty-somethings with printed out screengrabs of her videos. Rio ushered them forward, taking a sharpie that somebody offered to her as she started to sign the shots from her latest videos. “Thanks so much for coming out,” she would say with a wink to every fan. She also took a couple of selfies and flipped off the camera on request before giving them a wave goodbye as they giggled and shuffled away.

“Wow,” Agatha said, “you’re pretty popular, huh?”

Rio shrugged, blushing, and scratched the back of her neck. “A little bit,” she said. “Like maybe a T-list celebrity. S-list if we’re being generous.”

“We have a few hundred thousand followers on Tiktok,” Dulce said, proudly. “Only about twenty of those thousand are bots, I think.”

Jen let out a low whistle. “Impressive,” she said.

Rio saw the stars appear in her sister’s eyes immediately, a flush spreading over her entire face. She would tease her about that later.

“How are you doing, by the way?” Jen asked, leaning around Alice. “Been taking more photos?”

“Of course!” Dulce said, smiling bashfully. “I’m actually working on a series of rooftops shots around Westview. I’m trying to stitch together a skyline, actually, but there’s really not that many tall buildings in town for what I’m attempting to do.”

“Which is what, exactly?” Agatha asked, seeming genuinely interested.

Dulce was practically vibrating with excitement as she explained her project, which was originally going to be a panorama of the Westview skyline from one end of the town to the other, but it ended up turning into a stitch the same shot at different hours of the day from one singular rooftop (the tallest resident building in downtown Westview, which was only about six stories high) and how she was attempting to get 24 shots of that to put together.

“Obviously, spending twenty-four hours on a rooftop isn’t really that easy,” Dulce said, blushing and shrugging, “and I haven’t really been able to get a consistent enough shot for it to work as seamlessly as I’d hoped, but maybe if I choose a different location…”

“No,” Jen said. “No way. That’s a brilliant plan. That’s also my building you’re talking about.” She narrowed her gaze at Dulce. “Wait, how did you get rooftop access?”

Dulce’s eyes widened and her face blanched. “Uhhhh….”

“This girl got her Masters before she could legally drink, ladies and gentleman,” Rio said. Dulce glared and sent an elbow directly into her ribs at that. “Jeez!” Rio wheezed. Dulce had really put her soul into that one.

She was definitely still miffed.

“So,” Dulce said, looking between Agatha, Jen, and Rio, still semi-glaring at the latter, “how did you all meet?”

“Agatha and I met in college,” Jen said. “We had a chem class together. I double-majored so I ended up helping her and then we…” she shrugged, “eh, I guess you could say we become somewhat ‘friends’.” She used air quotes.

“You’re a bitch,” Agatha huffed.

“Love you,” Jen replied, cheerily as she held up both middle fingers. “We went into business after grad school. Well, actually, I got my PhD and then we went into business together.”

“Ooh, was that hard?” Dulce asked. “I’ve been thinking about getting my PhD.”

“You have ?” Rio asked, furrowing her brow. “You never told me that.”

“I guess we don’t tell each other everything, then, do we?” Dulce replied, coolly.

Okay, ouch. Rio deserved that.

Agatha and Alice both shot her questioning glances, but Jen didn’t seem to recognize the barb in Dulce’s response.

“You’d get one in photography?” she asked Dulce.

Dulce nodded. “I love taking photos, but I’m also super into photo-journalism and nature photography,” she explained. Both of these things Rio knew, though Dulce hadn’t really been focusing on them a lot as of late. Not that Rio was aware of, anyway. “I already have my Master’s, so I could probably do something with that, but there’s a certain level of prestige in being a Doctor , you know?”

“Girl, do I,” Jen laughed. “It might be worthwhile. You could even be on a research team while pursuing it. I know the head of the department at my alma mater, and I could probably get you in touch with her if you’re really serious about it.”

Dulce’s eyes nearly plopped out of her head, they went so wide. “Seriously?” she asked, her hands clasping together like a tiny child who had just been promised all the candy she could eat in her lifetime. “That would be amazing .”

“I mean, you’d still obviously have to put in the work,” Jen said, “but I’m sure that’s not a problem for you. I mean, you did break into my building, for which I pay my HOA handsomely to keep secure. How did you even do that?”

“I didn’t break into the building,” Dulce said. “Just onto the roof. The Starks live there, too. I just asked for Morgan’s help.” 

She motioned to Tony and Morgan behind the bar, the latter of which must have already been looking their way because she looked like a deer caught in headlights. She waved and gave them – especially Dulce – a shy, brace-filled smile.

“Okay, well how did she gain roof access?” Jen asked, offering the teen a wave back. “Because nobody’s supposed to be able to get up there.”

“Sorry,” Dulce said, “but I took a blood oath never to tell anybody the how.”

“ What ?” Rio asked, frowning at her. Dulce avoided her gaze.

Jen just nodded, sagely. “Respect,” she said. “If she can do it again, though, you can stay at my place for the twenty-four hours you’d need to get your shot.”

“Seriously?” Dulce asked, her voice breathy. “You…you’d let me do that?”

Jen shrugged. “You’re not a serial killer, right?” She eyed Rio.

“How am I supposed to know what this girl gets up to when she’s out of my sight? I’m not her keeper…anymore.”

Dulce rolled her eyes. “I’m not a serial killer,” Dulce promised, holding her hand up like a scout, three fingers raised.

She was never a scout.

“Are you a serial killer?” she asked Jen, narrowing her eyes almost playfully.

“I sure hope not,” Alice said from behind Jen’s shoulder. 

Jen offered her an affectionate smile, turning to wrap her arm around Alice’s waist. “I’m not a serial killer,” she cooed, “but I bet I could make you scream.”

There was a beat of silence in which Alice’s face turned bright red before the rest of the group let out groans of disgust, Agatha shoving Jen with a huff as she snickered, her attention still on Alice, who seemed to be completely malfunctioning.

“On that note,” Agatha said, “why don’t you two scram and go finish the rest of your date before you make the rest of us barf? I’m gonna grab a drink.” She turned to Rio. “What would you like?”

“Oh, I already have a tab open,” Rio said. “You can put it–”

“Nope,” Agatha said. “No way. I’m paying this time.”

“ This time?” Dulce asked, and Rio could hear the edge to her voice as she looked between them. Alice had already started tugging Jen toward the exit without so much as a goodbye. (Good for her, to be honest.) “When was the last time you went out for drinks?” 

“She bought me coffee yesterday,” Agatha explained before Rio could even open her mouth, “against my will.”

“That’s dramatic,” Rio huffed. “I was just quicker at paying. And it was way cheaper than anything you could get here, by the way.”

“Still,” Agatha said. “It’s my treat this time. Dulce, that goes for you, too, dear.”

Rio smirked when Dulce’s cheeks darkened in another blush and she cleared her throat. “Thank you, Miss Harkness,” she said.

“Hon,” Agatha said, a slightly warning tone to her voice as she looked at Dulce.

“Sorry!” Dulce said, holding her hands up in surrender. She cleared her throat. “Agatha,” she corrected.

Rio snickered under her breath and dodged Dulce’s elbow: she learned her lesson there.

“So,” Dulce said, once they were seated at a table by the bar, “how, exactly, did you two meet?” 

She had some fruity drink that looked like liquid cotton candy with a silly straw and reminded Rio of the Friendly’s they used to drive thirty minutes out of their way for on special occasions, like birthdays and graduations and days ending in Y. Agatha had a glass of Merlot, and Rio just had a Stella Artois. 

Agatha looked at Rio at the question, halfway through her first sip of wine. Rio looked back, pressing her lips to the lip of the bottle and taking a shallow sip. Dulce glanced between them like she was watching a silent tennis match.

“What?” she asked. “Did you meet at a sex club or something?”

Rio choked on her tiny sip of beer and she could swear some wine came out of Agatha’s nose when she snorted out a shocked laugh.

“ What ?” Agatha said. “Where on earth …?”

“Well, why else would you be hesitating this much?!” Dulce huffed, throwing her hands up. “I just want straight answers here!”

“Oh, honey,” Agatha said, reaching out to pat her hand, “if you want straight answers, ask a straight lady.” She winked at Dulce, who flushed and took a sip of her cotton candy monstrosity, which almost certainly had way more sugar than alcohol in it.

Rio pressed her lips together, ducking her head a little at the smile and wink Agatha shot her way. 

“You didn’t tell her?” Agatha asked, after she’d finished dabbing the wine from her lips. Rio shook her head. “Why not?”

“It’s not my place to tell your business,” Agatha admitted, giving Dulce an apologetic smile. “Sorry, Duls.” 

“Well, that’s considerate of you,” Agatha said, giving Rio a warm smile. “But it’s really not necessary. I’m not ashamed of it.”

“Ashamed of what?” Dulce asked. “Did something happen?” She was looking only at Agatha now.

Agatha nodded. “I was diagnosed,” she said, her words slow and a little drawn-out, her hand tensing around the stemless wine glass she held just slightly, “with…MS. Rio and I met at our MS group.” She took a deep breath and another sip. Under the table, Rio’s foot brushed hers and Agatha glanced at her as she sipped.

“Oh,” Dulce said, her shoulders relaxing a little bit as she looked between Agatha and Rio, her expression softening as she regarded her sister. Rio gave her a tight-lipped smile. “Oh, wow,” she said. “That really sucks. I…I had no idea.”

“Well, how could you have any idea?” Agatha asked with a slight chuckle. “ I didn’t even have any idea. I wouldn’t have, either, had it not been for the fact that my left hand went numb last year and left me unable to paint. Temporarily,” she hastened to add when Dulce’s eyes went wide and her mouth gaped slightly. “I regained feeling before I even saw the neurologist. I thought it was just a side effect from a flu shot.” She shrugged. “I was wrong, of course. I know that now.” She looked down into the nearly empty glass. Rio reached over to place her hand on Agatha’s arm, and Agatha jumped slightly at the action. Rio was about to remove her hand, but found Agatha’s fingers wrapped around hers before she could.

She met her bright blue gaze with her own and they shared a long look before Agatha let go and drained the rest of her glass. 

“I’m going to get another,” she said. “Anybody else want something while I’m gone?”

“No, thanks,” Rio said, holding up her half-full beer.

“I’m okay,” Dulce said. Most of her drink was still there. The straw made consumption slow.

“Okay,” Agatha said. “I’m gonna close out so this is your last chance.” She stood next to the table, eyeing each of them in turn, giving them one last chance to place their order.”

“I should actually go pretty soon,” Dulce said. “I have an early shift. I’m just gonna finish this.”

“Eat something when you get home,” Rio said, “before you fall asleep.”

“Duh,” Dulce huffed, rolling her eyes like a petulant teenager. But she was also grinning affectionately. Rio mirrored her smile.

“Brat,” she said as Agatha stepped away from the table. She leaned in. “Do you understand now,” she asked, “why I couldn’t say anything?”

“Yeah,” Dulce sighed. “I get it.” She eyed Agatha as she signed the receipt and laughed at something Morgan was saying. “So, you guys met at group?”

“Yeah,” Rio confirmed. “On Monday.”

“You only just met on Monday ?” Dulce hissed. “I thought you’d been keeping this secret from me for at least , like, a month !”

“I would never !” Rio scoffed. “I mean, I absolutely would if Agatha wanted me to.”

“Oh, I see,” Dulce said, with a knowing smirk, “you’re smitten.”

Rio coughed up half her sip of beer at that, reaching for napkins to hastily wipe her face. “What?” she wheezed. “I am not .”

“Oh, you totally are,” Dulce said. “Don’t try to deny it. She’s the girl in the park, isn’t she?”

Rio’s eyes widened at that, her jaw dropping as Dulce took another sip of her drink through that ridiculous silly straw, her lips curved up in a knowing smirk.

“What about the park?” Agatha asked, setting her glass down before perching on her own stool at the high-top table.

“I think I might take a walk through it tomorrow,” Dulce said, “on my lunch break. Maybe I’ll go visit my floral niblings. Rio loves them more than she does me, you know.”

“They’re my babies,” Rio said, unapologetically.

“So, if we were all trapped in a burning building, you’d save them over me?” Dulce gasped.

“That’s not fair,” Rio whined. “They don’t have legs! Besides, I’m the one that walks with a cane. I’d be relying on you to save me !”

“Touché,” Dulce said, tipping her mostly empty glass at Rio. “Anyway, I think I’m gonna head out. Thank you for the drink, Mis–ahem, Agatha . It was nice to see you again, though I’m sure I’ll be seeing more of you now that you and my sister are,” she eyed Rio, “friends.”

Agatha squinted at that pause, but she said nothing as she took another sip of her wine. Meanwhile, Dulce stood and brought her mostly empty glass to the bar. Rio watched with a smirk as Morgan shoved her dad away and smiled brightly as Dulce approached. The girls said something to each other and laughed before Dulce gave Morgan a little wave and headed to the door.

Rio shook her head as Morgan gazed at her sister’s retreating form, her smile a little dazed. Tony stepped back up next to her and poked her in the side, murmuring something in her ear that made her turn and shove him in response. He just laughed, wrapping his arms around her and pressing a kiss to her forehead.

“So, your sister is kind of intense, huh?” Agatha asked, after a moment of silence. 

“Yeah,” Rio chuckled. “It’s the Vidal family trait, I guess.”

“You’re not that intense,” Agatha snorted. “I don’t think she blinked once your entire show.”

“Oh, yeah,” Rio said, smiling bashfully, “uh…about that. She does that when she’s pissed.”

Agatha furrowed her brow. “Pissed? Like angry?” Rio nodded, taking a sip of her now-lukewarm beer. What did she have to be angry about?”

“The fact that I didn’t tell her that you and I, uh,” Rio swallowed thickly, “met. I mean, like, that we were sorta hanging out.”

“Oh.” Agatha tilted her head. “Why, exactly, would she care about that?”

“Because you’re, like, her role model,” Rio said, knowing that if Dulce was there, she’d strangle her with a beer hose. “She really looks up to you, you know, for being a business owner and a successful artist.” She drained the last dregs of her beer. “Don’t ever tell her I told you that or you’ll never find my body.”

“Don’t you mean they’ll never find my body?” Agatha snorted.

“No,” Rio said, gravely serious. “Dulce would decimate me if she found out I said those words to you. There probably wouldn’t even be a body to find .”

Agatha didn’t laugh at that, but she did smirk into her next sip of wine, shaking her head.

“She seems like a great kid,” Agatha said. “Funny and charming.”

“And intense?” Rio chuckled. 

“Well, those things aren’t mutually exclusive, it would seem,” Agatha said, her voice a little low, warm. 

Rio felt her insides go equally warm, and she began to play with the label on her beer, peeling it off easily with the help of the condensation. Honestly, she didn’t really know what else to say to that: she wasn’t all that great at talking about herself, except briefly or in front of an audience, for a laugh, but to talk about Dulce?

She’d never made jokes about her sister or spoke about her when she wasn’t around to interject. It made Rio feel uncomfortable. That may have honestly been because the only time she spoke about Dulce growing up was to her teachers (who always gushed about how smart and creative she was) or her teachers (who complained that Dulce didn’t treat them with the respect they think they deserved just for being the people who supplied their genetic material to her despite pawning her off on their eldest to raise her). 

She liked to brag about her sometimes, but those conversations could get tiresome. And tonight wasn’t about bragging about her genius little sister. Tonight was about them . Her and Agatha.

Is there even a you and Agatha? that asshole voice inside her head asked.

She glanced back up at the other woman and found Agatha already looking at her, her head tilted. Her smirk, too.

“What?” Rio asked, her cheeks going hot.

Agatha shrugged and shook her head. “Nothing,” she said. “I just…I don’t think I’ve ever seen you stay quiet for this long.”

“You calling me a blabbermouth, Harkness?” Rio shot back, giving her an easy grin in return. “I talk too much?”

“Not at all,” Agatha laughed. The sound was throaty and light. That second glass of wine had really loosened her up. She probably wasn’t drunk though. Just buzzed. But a little bit more unguarded than usual. “I actually like it,” Agatha admitted, “when you lecture about certain subjects. Have you ever thought about being a professor?”

“Like, at a college?” Rio asked, lifting a brow. “What would I even teach?”

“Don’t you have a Master’s in botany?” Agatha asked, tipping her empty glass toward Rio. “Couldn’t you teach that?”

Rio shrugged. “Probably,” he said. “Most universities are looking for people with PhDs, though. I’d probably be an adjunct, at best.”

“That could be fun,” Agatha said. “I’m sure your students would love you and your lectures.”

“You really think so?” Rio asked, feeling something flutter in her chest. 

“You have a natural stage presence and knowledge of not only botany, but a great deal of other things. You’ve taught me more about chocolate than I ever knew there was to know,” she said. 

They both laughed that time, their chuckles mingling almost musically to Rio’s ears. 

“I guess you might have a point,” she said. “You know, you could also be a professor. You have a Master’s, too, right?”

“Two, technically,” Agatha said, a bit bashfully. “I primarily wanted a degree in art history, but I’d double-majored in business in my undergrad, so I figured why not do the same at grad school.” She shuddered. “Horrible experience. Would not reccommend. Those two years were hell .”

“Need another glass?” Rio said, standing up, motioning to her wine.

“No,” Agatha said, shaking her head. “No, I shouldn’t. I still haven’t even eaten dinner, actually. This is just gonna go straight through me.”

“Wanna grab a slice next door?” Rio asked, nodding toward the door. “Best pizza in Westview.”

“That’s a high bar,” Agatha retorted, dryly, rolling her eyes with a snort. “Um, sure, I guess. Not like I can really drive home right now, anyway. Let me just…” She held up her cup. Rio nodded, grabbing her cane as Agatha walked the glass back over to the bar. 

Morgan Stark took it from her with a bright smile. That kid was like pure sunshine where her father was typically the silent, surly type. Oh, Tony Stark could be charming when he wanted to be, but he was nowhere near the level of sunny disposition of his daughter. 

Agatha laughed at something Morgan said before giving her a little wave and walked over to meet Rio halfway to the door.

Rio held out her arm as Rio got closer. “M’lady,” she said with a little bow, her other had clutching her cane to keep her upright. Her legs were really starting to feel the exhuastion from all the times she’d forced herself to walk around tonight. Damn Dulce and her unblinking eyes. She tried not to let it show as Agatha took the offered arm like a lady in the Regency era, ducking her head a little so that her dark curls hid her face slightly.

Rio could still see her smile and that blush, though.

Damn, she was beautiful.

Thankfully, it didn’t take much walking to get them to Pizz-a-Westview (pronounced “Piece of Westview” though there were many who called it “Piss a Westview. Rio may or may not have been included in this ‘many’) and Rio was able to take a seat close to the door, sweating slightly.

“Are you okay?” Agatha asked, her brows furrowing in concern as she looked down at Rio, who was rubbing her left thigh, attempting to get the feeling back in her leg. 

“I’m fine,” Rio assured her. “I just…um, there’s a reason I’m called the sit-down comedian, you know?” She took a deep, shuddering breath as she stretched her legs out under the table. “I should be fine in a minute or two, but I really gave my muscles a workout that my nerves can’t exactly keep up with. But I’m fine.”

Agatha looked like she wanted to ask another “are you sure” but she only pressed her lips together and nodded again, taking the seat across from Rio just as a teen girl appeared next to the table.

“Hey, Miss Rio,” the girl greeted, giving Rio a dap as she placed a menu on the table, pointedly just sliding it toward Agatha. “How was your set tonight?”

“I think I did pretty well,” Rio said. “Agatha here seemed to like it.”

The girl, whose nametag read ‘Shuri’ turned to look at Agatha.

Agatha shrugged. “It was okay,” she said, but Rio could see the mischievous twinkle in her eyes. Still, she acted hurt, placing her hand on her chest as if wounded.

“Et tu, Agaté?” she said, dramatically.

Shuri snorted while Agatha rolled her eyes and plucked up the menu. 

“The usual tonight, Miss Rio?” she asked.

“Yes, please,” Rio said. “Thanks.”

“And you, Miss…Agatha, was it? You need another moment with the menu?”

“Just Agatha is fine, dear,” Agatha said. “Are these personal pizzas?”

“Yes,” Shuri answered. “They’re about the size of a frisbee. We can also prepare a Medium for you to share or I can give you one of our pre-made slices from the back of the menu. Everything is available right now.”

Agatha turned the menu over, her crystal blue eyes perusing it for a long moment before landing on something she seemed to like. She glanced up at Rio before leaning toward Shuri to show her what she wanted. Shuri nodded, sagely.

“Good choice,” she said, taking the menu. “Anything to drink?”

Again, she was only looking at Agatha: she knew what Rio liked to drink.

Agatha glanced behind the clear display case at the register, which showed off all the different pre-made pizzas, and through to where there was a soda fountain.

“Coke?” she asked. 

“Coming right up,” Shuri said, turning on her heel to make her way to the back of the pizza shop, where there were already several women rolling dough in flour or topping the various sizes of pizza or answering the phones, which rang off the hook on Saturday nights.

“I’ve never seen so many women working at a pizza place,” Agatha murmured. “Usually, it’s a bunch of sweaty, hairy men.”

“Ramonda has an all-female staff,” Rio informed her. “That’s Shuri’s mother. She’s the owner.”

“She named this place?” Agatha asked, glancing at the neon sign on the window.

Rio let out a laugh, shaking her head. “No way,” she said. “Her husband named it.” She frowned as her chest tightened. “He passed last year. They didn’t have the heart to rename it. For as much shit as he got from the local teens over the name, T’Chaka was proud of his shop and the name that made his children giggle when they first moved here from Wakanda. Ramonda didn’t have the heart to change it after his passing.”

Agatha nodded, solemnly. “It’s a good name,” she said. “Very much like what I’d imagine a father would name his pizza place.”

“Their son, T’Challa, is at university right now, but he usually runs it right alonside his mother. He’s in school for business, too.”

“And how old is Shuri?” Agatha whispered, leaning in. “Isn’t it a little late for her to be working?”

“She’s sixteen,” Rio whispered back, “and it’s only a quarter to eleven. Since it’s Saturday, she can work until midnight tonight. Besides, she’s already graduated.”

“She’s only sixteen and she’s already graduated high school?” Agatha asked. She pressed her lips together when Shuri came back, placing a Coke in front of her and a Sprite in front of Rio. Agatha offered her a thankful smile.

Rio saluted her with her glass. 

When she was out of earshot, she gave Agatha a grin. “Shuri has her Bachelor’s in Engineering, actually,” she said. “She’s taking a gap year before grad school to relax.”

Agatha’s eyes widened at that. “Why do you surround yourself with such intelligent toddlers?”

“They’re good company,” Rio replied with a grin. “Shuri and Dulce met while Duls was doing her final year of grad school. “She was only thirteen back then. Dulce kind of took Shuri under her wing. They had completely different majors, obviously, but Dulce knew what it was like to be the little kid amongst the bigger ones. She wanted to protect Shuri from a lot of the mistakes she’d made her freshman and sophomore year (for Shuri, this was pretty much the same year of school because the girl is a super genius).”

“Aww,” Agatha said. “That’s sweet. What is in the drinking water in Westview? And why didn’t I get any of it?”

“I think it’s the pizza that made Shuri so smart. Wait until you try it.”

“Order up!” 

As if on cue, Shuri appeared with a tray of two personal pizzas. She placed a pepperoni and sausage down in front of Rio. “Your regular, madam,” she said, presenting it with a bow. 

“Mercí,” Rio replied, rubbing her hands together as she licked her lips, hungrily. Her stomach was growling like a lion. She never ate before shows because she didn’t want anything to upset her stomach if she got nervous. It would be way too embarrassing to have to run off to use the bathroom in the middle of a set. Sure , she could make it into a funny bit, but that bit would get old way too fast if she took a long time indisposed. 

Better to not risk it.

Usually, she would have a hot burger waiting for her, courtesy of the Starks, after the show, but she’d asked them to forgo it tonight. She knew, somehow, that she and Agatha would end up here.

She just didn’t know that it would take so long. Now she was famished .

“And for Miss Agatha,” Shuri said–

–“Agatha” Agatha interjected. Shuri ignored her. 

“A Hawaiian pizza,” Shuri finished, placing the ham and pineapple monstrosity down in front of Agatha. 

“Your betrayal keeps getting deeper ,” Rio gasped, recoiling from the woman behind her in mock – no, very, very real – horror. “How could you? And in my safe space, of all places!”

“Hey,” Agatha huffed, trying and failing to bite back a grin as she looked down at her abomination before God, “I like ham, I like pineapple, and I like pizza. Why not combine all three? It just seems more convenient.”

“It’s an affront to God and all decency !” Rio huffed. “Right, Shuri?”

“Mother says I am not allowed to give my personal opinion in any way that might lose us business,” Shuri said, folding her arms behind her back like the dutiful daughter that she was. “But I will say that I do believe karma is real and it will come for you soon, Miss Agatha. Enjoy your pizzas! Let me know if you need anything else!”  

With that, she was off to cater to the few other tables that had seated themselves since Agatha and Rio’s arrival. Rio just shook her head at Agatha as she took the first slice of her atrocious pizza and brought it to her mouth, blowing slightly to cool it off.

She used to joke with Alice about what it would take for a crush to die. Most women she’d had a crush on could do just about anything to her and she would thank them. There were only really three things one could do that would be a dealbreaker for her.

Number one was to be rude to waitstaff or customer service workers in general. 

Rio could not stand people who were rude to the workers at any store for pretty much any reason. She had scooped ice cream in high school. Her sister was a barista. They had worked hard at their jobs to make minimum wage, but they’d both had people scream in their faces about things they literally could not control. They’d also had people make little digs at them and undervalue them for the positions they held. In Rio’s opinion, that was just as bad.

All three times Rio had seen Agatha interact with somebody in a position of service in just the last couple of days, she had proven herself to be a kind and decent person, especially to the younger workers, like Shuri and Kamala. 

Score one for Agatha.

The second was to be rude or unkind to her sister.

Dulce was sweet and kind and bubbly and energetic. She could be a lot sometimes, especially when she was a little kid. Rio would – and has – cut off anybody who couldn’t deal with that energy. Friends, girlfriends…it didn’t matter. Dulce was her number one. Forever. She didn’t let snide remarks or backhanded compliments slide off her back. She’d once left a date because the girl had called her sister ‘too much’ after Dulce had made her a drawing of the three of them from the park a week earlier.

Who says that about a little kid’s drawing? That shit is adorable! Rio had exclaimed, recounting the story to Alice years later. She was still very much mad about it, and how the girl had laughed when Rio had warned her not to say shit like that in front of her, like she thought it was a joke.

Rio had very much not been joking.

Agatha had been nothing but nice to Dulce since the moment they met (Dulce would not shut up about how nice Agatha Harkness is after her showcase), and it was obvious that she had affection for the younger artist.

Score two for Agatha.

The third was Hawaiian Pizza.

Rio had gotten into heated debates in high school over this very subject. Hawaiian Pizza wasn’t even Hawaiian ! It was invented in Canada ! They had no right to slap pineapple on a pizza and then ascribe it to a people who had absolutely nothing to do with the ruination of two of Rio’s favorite things (pineapple itself was fine, and she obviously loved pizza). It was like slapping some plantains on a plate of spaghetti and calling it Puerto Rican Lasagna .

She did not like it. In high school, she had tried to get a petition going that straight up banned it from Westview in its entirety. 

Obviously, it did not work.

But Rio had always maintained that anybody who actively chose to partake in the grotesque oddity that was “Hawaiian” pizza was not to be trusted.

Until now.

Because Agatha Harkness looked absolutely adorable munching on her pizza. She was making happy noises as she popped pieces of pineapple straight from the sea of cheese and into her mouth, waggling her head like there was a jaunty little tune playing in her mind as she ate.

Usually, seeing somebody enjoy Satan’s Birthday Cake like that would have sent her on a tirade, but there was something about Agatha’s joy at her absolutely revolting little treat that was actively charming Rio. She almost wanted to ask for a bite.

But then she took another look at Agatha’s dish and wrinkled her nose in disgust.

No. Not a chance. She’d simply let Agatha enjoy the whole thing all on her own.

Rio swallowed thickly as she dug into her own pizza, attempting to avert her gaze from Agatha’s so that her mind didn’t drink her into thinking that her pepperoni were little slices of ham or that the chunks of sausage were actually pineapple bits. That was all she needed tonight.

Even if that did happen, though, she knew she could never hold it against Agatha. As much and for as long as she had said that liking Hawaiian pizza was a dealbreaker for her, it felt different when the person who liked it was Agatha Harkness.

Rio grinned as she took a bite of her pizza.

Damn her.

 

“I can’t believe you’re going to take that abomination home with you,” Rio huffed as Shuri handed Agatha a box for the last few slices of her “pizza”. “You’re really going to warm that thing up tomorrow and make it taste even more gross?”

“Actually, I like to eat it cold,” Agatha responded, grinning when Rio let out a little gagging sound. Troll .

She was doing this on purpose just to get a rise out of Rio.

Rio hated that she didn’t hate it.

She put her own remaining three slices into the box. Usually, she could finish a whole personal pizza like this and still have room for dessert, but this time the fluttering in her stomach every time she looked at Agatha made it hard to eat everything.

It could have also been the nausea that Hawaiian “pizza” induces, as well.

Okay, maybe she was being a bit dramatic about this.

She really did think it was the devil, though. She was justified in that.

“Have a nice night!” Shuri said, starting to sweep the floor and wipe down the tables for closing time.

“Don’t we have to pay?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

“Miss Rio took care of it, already,” Shuri informed her. “Slipped me her card under the table when I came by for refills.”

“You little…” Agatha huffed, glaring at Rio, who just grinned and shrugged. 

“It was my turn to pay after you bought the drinks,” Rio said. “Fair is fair.”

“That beer was, like, six dollars max !” Agatha exclaimed. “This meal was fifteen !”

“You also bought my little sister a drink,” Rio reminded her. “It was definitely more than ten, so actually I still owe you a little bit to make us even.”

“No way,” Agatha said. “I’m buying lobster next time.”

“ Next time ?” Rio teased, grabbing her cane and hobbling toward the door with her pizza in her other hand. “A little presumptuous, don’t you think. Especially after making me watch you eat that… thing .”

“If you don’t stop, I’ll bring you to a pizza shop that only serves Hawaiian pizza and won’t let you leave until you’ve had a whole slice of it,” Agatha threatened, rushing ahead of Rio to open the door for her.

“I’m pretty sure that goes against the Geneva Conventions,” Rio said, walking out onto the street.

“Y’all are too much,” Shuri said, laughing behind them as they left. “See you later, Miss Rio! Hope to see you back soon, Miss Agatha!”

“You too, dear!” Agatha replied, sunnily. She turned to Rio as soon as the door was closed. “You need a ride home?” she asked, reaching for her car keys clipped to her belt loop on a little purple carabiner.

“I don’t live very far away from here, actually,” Rio said. “I can walk home.”

“Don’t be ridiculous,” Agatha said, pressing a button on the little remote. An orange car about five feet away blinked awake. “Wouldn’t want your leg to give out on you.”

“That’s a bit ableist.”

“It very much is not,”  Agatha laughed, tugging her by the arm to the orange Subaru. “You could barely make it to the pizza shop a couple hours ago.”

“But I’ve had sustenance since then,” Rio reminded her, holding up her leftover pizza. “I’m sure I’ll be fine.”

“Are you even okay to drive?” Rio asked. “You seemed a little tipsy before.”

“I’m better now,” Agatha said. “Time and pizza helped. I might have a headache in the morning. Just get in.”

“Jeez, okay!” Rio laughed, walking around to the passenger side door and slipping into the car. “I really don’t live that far though.”

“So this should be a short trip. Just sit back and enjoy the ride.”

Rio felt her face go warm at that as Agatha started up the car. She cleared her throat and looked out the window as she pulled away from the curb. Most other cars were gone, the spots taken up only by the few with overnight parking passes to avoid the meters and parking tickets. The street was pretty quiet and empty, even the bar.

It only took a minute to get to Rio’s apartment.

“I’m right here,” she said, pointing to her building, which was, give or take, about two hundred feet from The Witches’ Road .

“You’re kidding,” Agatha said. 

“I told you I live close,” Rio laughed. “You should have listened to me.”

“I didn’t think you meant ‘ across the street’ close!” Agatha exclaimed, but she was also laughing. 

They sat there in Agatha’s car for a long time, just laughing at the absurdity of it all. Rio probably could have hobbled to her building faster than it took Agatha to start the car, shift gears, and pull out into the street, but she had done what was asked and humored her.

“Thanks for the ride, anyway,” Rio said, shrugging one shoulder as unbuckled her seatbelt. 

“Wait,” Agatha said, “let me walk you to your door.” She turned off the engine and put her hazards on.

“That’s really not that far, either,” Rio informed her. “I have an ADA-compliant apartment on the first floor. It’s literally fifty feet from the front entrance.”

“And I will walk you that fifty feet,” Agatha said, stubbornly. “Let’s go.”

Rio rolled her eyes fondly as the other woman jumped out before she could protest. “What a gentleman,” she murmured as she slipped out with her cane and her pizza. 

She met Agatha on the sidewalk and the two walked toward the entrance of her building, their shoulders brushing as they went. Rio reached for her building fob, waving it in front of the automatic doors.

“Wow,” Agatha commented, “electric doorman.”

Rio snorted. “More ADA-compliance,” she said. “Makes it easier for people in wheelchairs or walking with aids to smoothly get into the apartment.”

“Nice,” Agatha said. “When did you move in here?”

“Around the time this happened,” she said, holding up her cane for a second. “But that was just good timing. It can take a really long time for these kinds of apartments to open up. We were already on the waitlist for this building because we had Section 8. I updated them about the change in my needs and they were like ‘dope we have the perfect place for you’ and the rest is history. It’s a pretty cool place.”

“Seems cool,” Agatha said as they walked through the lobby, which had mailboxes along one wall, none of them higher that a relatively short person’s eye level. 

Rio led her to the left hallway, where the apartment she shared with Dulce was, literally, the first door on the right, next to the elevator. 

“This is me,” she said, “again.”

“Wow,” Agatha said. “You weren’t kidding about it only being about fifty feet.”

“Fifty feet exactly,” Rio said, grinning. “The landlord told me that the first day, like it was the biggest selling point. Didn’t hurt, to be honest.”

Agatha nodded, biting her lower lip as she turned toward Rio, who was suddenly made nervous by the way Agatha was looking at her and playing with the sleeves of her cardigan. It looked really soft. She wished her hands weren’t full so she could feel the material. It was probably really smooth and cool and…

Agatha leaned into her space, but stopped a few inches from their noses brushing as if restraining herself, her blue eyes searching Rio’s, asking a question that Rio was desperate to say yes to.

Before she could, however, the door opened and they were practically both knocked over by Dulce making a hasty exit from the apartment.

“Oops!” Dulce said. “Sorry, I didn’t mean to– Agatha? What are you doing here?” She glanced over to her sister. Rio could feel her face flaming as she stood, wide-eyed like a robber caught red-handed, holding her leftover pizza. “Rio? What’s going…?”

Dulce looked between them and her genius brain processed everything she was seeing in milliseconds, her lips upturning in a very “You like Krabby Patties, don’t you, Squidward?” kind of way.

Rio immediately gave her a Look that said “Do not fuck with me right now, cockblock” and Dulce raised her hands in surrender.

“Sorry,” she said. “I’m just heading out.”

“What?” Rio asked. “I thought you had a morning shift.”

“I got Tommy to switch with me,” Dulce said. “Morgan’s gonna let me on the roof again and Miss Kale said I can come to her apartment when I need a break…in the afternoon, anyway. She said she’ll be a bit…busy until then.”

“Ew,” Agatha and Rio said in unison. Then shared a shy grin.

Dulce looked between them and rolled her eyes. Hard.

“Anyway,” she said, “ this apartment is gonna be empty for the next few hours, though, so…have fun!”

Then she rushed past them without another word, her overnight bag slung over her shoulder, the door to the apartment still half-open.

Swan poked her head outside, meowing gruffly up at the two women in the doorway. Reaper was behind her, tilting her head curiously with that permanently smiling face of hers.

“Who’s this?” Agatha asked, smiling as she crouched down in front of the fat cat. She scratched under Swan’s chin, immediately gaining her favor. 

“That’s Swan,” Rio said, swallowing thickly. “She’s a sweetheart. The other one is Reaper.”

“Swan,” Agatha echoed. “Reaper.” She glanced at the other cat. “Well, that fits,” she said, eyeing the skull-like pattern on Reaper’s face. “But why is this one Swan?”

“It’s short for Ron Swanson,” Rio informed her. “He’s a character on this show Dulce and I used to watch, Parks and Recreation . We just saw her and knew that was her name.”

“That’s adorable,” Agatha said. “I’ve never seen that show.”

“Seriously!?” Rio gasped. She’d rarely met somebody who hasn’t seen at least part of Parks and Rec . “We have to watch it!”

“Rain check on that?” Agatha said, standing back up. Her knees didn’t crack or anything, damn runner. “I need to get back out there before my car gets towed.”

“Sure,” Rio said, her heart swelling with the knowledge that this meant she would definitely see Agatha Harkness again, outside of group therapy. Again. “It’s a date.”

“Yeah,” Agatha said, nodding decisively, “it is.”

They stood there for another long moment, just staring at each other, smiling like idiots but neither making any move, either toward each other or away.

“Well,” Agatha said, “I’ll, um, text you tomorrow, okay?”

“Okay,” Rio said, clearing her throat as she nudged Swan inside the apartment with her foot. Swan looked up at her with the most scandalized expression, as though Rio had just insulted her entire ancestry. But she went inside like a good girl. Reaper welcomed her with grooming licks to her shattered little ego.

Rio started to move into the apartment, but before she could get too far, she felt Agatha’s hand hook around her elbow, causing her to turn around.

She started to ask “what” but no sooner had the first consonant sound left her lips than they were covered by Agatha’s.

The kiss was brief and almost-chaste except for the barest hint of tongue swiping across Rio’s bottom lip. She didn’t even have time to deepen it before Agatha was pulling away, taking several steps until her back hit the opposite wall, her cheeks pink and blue eyes wide, her chest heaving a little bit.

“Um,” Agatha said, “thank you for the pizza. I’ll…bye!”

And then she was gone, her steps quick across the lobby to the front door, leaving Rio staring after her, mouth tingling more than her leg.

Chapter End Notes

I really hope the parts that I found funny came off as that way to you because I legit cracked myself up during this chapter.

I'm trying to catch up to my promise of one chapter per week for Disability Pride Month. I have one more to go by Friday to keep it. It may be shorter, but I hope you liked the 9k chapter here. Also, who guessed Swan's full name??
