Chapter 11: Something to Do

Chapter Summary

Agatha thinks about decisions she's made and decisions she's yet to make.

Just for fun, she drags Jen along for the ride.

Chapter Notes

My ADHD is acting up and I am finding it very hard to focus on writing. Not that I don't have the motivation to write, mind you, but my brain latches onto shiny things in my peripheral like I'm some kind of oddly-shaped crow with my head on a swivel. I'm gonna try to make the updates more regular, but I can't really make any promises because I know me too well and Me is kind of a mess.

That being said, I hope you enjoy this chapter because I feel as though it's a bit of a rollercoaster.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Eleven

Agatha couldn't remember the drive home.

Everything was fuzzy, blurred, soft at the edges — and it had nothing to do with the two glasses of wine she'd drunk earlier that evening.

Well, okay, maybe it had something to do with the alcohol that must have still been buzzing in her system. But it had been at least two hours since she'd finished the second glass and she now had her pizza to soak it up in her stomach. Agatha looked down at the box in her left hand. When she left the pizza shop, she'd been full, but now…

Ugh, she was always weirdly hungry when she was buzzed.

And when she got stressed.

She didn't really know which one was causing her hunger now; it was probably a combination of the two.

She had kissed Rio.

It barely counted as a kiss, though.

It was barely the lightest brush of lips.

And a slight swipe of her tongue over Rio's bottom lip.

But then she'd pulled away.

Just as Rio's lips had begun to move against hers.

That was probably a dumb decision.

Agatha opened the box and pulled out one of the remaining slices of pizza, bringing it up to her lips as she kicked off her shoes and padded toward the kitchen, where she deposited the box in the fridge. It was best to remove temptation.

She continued to munch on her mostly-cold pizza as she padded around the first floor of her house. She didn't feel tired enough to go up to bed just yet. Quite the opposite, actually. Her legs felt fuzzy, like an electric current was running through them, but it was too late to go running.

So there was only one thing to do.

Agatha's studio was quiet as she stepped inside. Of course it was. It was nearly midnight now. Westview as a whole was asleep, even on a Saturday night.

The trees just outside her backyard fence swayed in the breeze, creating shadows through the wide windows with the warm streetlights behind them. Agatha watched the shapes move across the room for a moment before she flicked on the lights and walked to the loveseat, slipping her arms from her cardigan and laying it over the back.

Her easel sat in the center of the room, as always, with a prepped, but blank, canvas waiting for her. She'd set up her paints days ago, certain that she'd find the time to start painting the sketch she'd made a few days ago, which was clipped to the edge of her easel, waiting for her to copy it onto the canvas.

She'd just left them sitting in their tubes, her pencil resting on the easel, still perfectly sharpened from disuse. Agatha sat down on her stool and began to copy what she'd sketched over a week ago now.

She worked diligently, occasionally stepping back from the stool to get a wider perspective and make sure that everything was proportionate. The figure of the woman she drew was the hardest part — specifically her hair.

Agatha didn't know if she should draw her with short hair or long hair. Should it be kept up or left loose, as it had been in her sketch. She started to draw it tied up in an elaborate bun, but that didn't seem to fit. So she erased that and sketched it as it was in the drawing, wild and loose around the figure's shoulders, but there was something off about that, as well.

Agatha let out a groan of frustration and placed her pencil right back down, feeling silly. It was just hair. What did it matter if it was up or down or tied or loose or…whatever?! It wasn't even the focus of the piece. That was meant to be the sun.

Or the woman?

Or the way the water lapped around her shins? Agatha hadn't even realized that she'd made the tide higher on the woman's body than it had been in the sketch. It was inching toward her knees, the beach swallowed up by a high tide.

Agatha stepped back from the outline of the piece and stared at the woman's head. She hadn't done much for it. It was just meant to be a guide for the hair that was supposed to fall over her shoulders and stick out wildly, like the ocean breeze had tousled it. She drew the faint outline of pierced ears sticking out at either side, with hoops hugging the shells.

Suddenly, Agatha didn't like the angle of the woman's currently-bald head.

She erased it and sketched it at a ¾ angle, facing away from the observer, enough to see part of the woman's profile. She drew the uneven slope of a nose that hooked a little bit at the end, long lashes over a half-lidded eye that was looking back, over the figure's shoulder, and what could only be described as a joyless smile. It curved just slightly upward, but the singular eyebrow Agatha drew was…sad. Together, it looked as though the woman was on the verge of tears.

Agatha didn't sketch any tears in the singular pale eye.

She placed her pencil down and stepped away, leaving the figure without hair still.

She was done for the night.

She placed the pencil back down on the easel and made her way quickly to the door, sparing only a cursory glance at the photograph on her wall, finally recognizing the shape of Rio's grin in the shadow of Dulce's photograph. Her heart hammered in her chest as she flicked off the lights, plunging the whole room into darkness.

 

 

Agatha didn't expect to see Jen less than twenty-four hours after the woman had been dragged out of the bar by a tiny rocker about half her size for some…fun.

In her bedroom.

Sitting at the end of her bed, eyes wide as she waited for Agatha to open hers.

Agatha practically fell out of the bed at the sight of Jen sitting there, holding two to-go mugs of coffee, a bright smile stretching her lips.

"What the fuck are you doing in my house?!" Agatha growled, pulling the covers up to her chest as if she were naked (she was not; she had on a pair of cotton pajamas that she'd slipped into after leaving her art studio just a few hours prior) and glared at the other woman.

"You weren't answering your phone," Jen said with a shrug. She held out one of the coffees and Agatha took it, reaching for her cell phone at the same time as she pushed herself into a sitting position. She blinked at the bright screen in her otherwise dark bedroom.

It was nearly noon, and she had about a dozen missed calls from Jen. And she'd missed every alarm she'd set. So much for her run.

She could miss a single day, she guessed, her body still fully rejecting being conscious even as she took a sip of coffee. Agatha let out a moan — it was Jen's fancy scmancy expensive brew. Damn her.

"I figured you'd be stuck in bed all day," Agatha murmured, smirking around the rim of her travel mug. "Or was Alice not all you hoped?"

"Oh, she was more," Jen replied, sighing dreamily, resting her chin in her hand. "That shaky hand of hers really comes in handy." She wiggled her eyebrows, and Agatha made a face. "It's like she has settings," Jen explained further.

"Ew! Jen!" Agatha huffed, wrinkling her nose. "Please spare me the details." She took another sip of the bougie-ass coffee. "Why aren't you with her right now if she's so great?"

Jen sighed. "Her mother called her in for rehearsal," Jen informed her, pouting. "They have to figure out how to work around her tremors for the tour dates she's going on with them, you know? If it's going to affect the sound of the songs." She shrugged. "But we're having dinner tonight, so I might be a little late getting into the office tomorrow."

"Don't you usually get there at, like, six AM anyway? For your stupid yoga shit? It's fine if you're a little late. America can handle the morning rush on her own, can't she?"

"Oh, she's more than capable," Jen agreed. "But I might be even later than you tomorrow. Unless, that is, you and Rio have similar plans tonight…?"

She raised her eyebrows until they reached the nonexistent hairline as she let the question hang in the air and took another sip of her own coffee.

"We don't," Agatha said. "She hasn't even texted me."

Jen deflated a little bit. "That's disappointing," she said. "I thought you two might have had a similar night to mine, but then Rio texted Alice this morning and she said it seemed like she was alone, so…"

Agatha took another slow sip of her coffee as Jen eyed her over the rim of her own.

"So…?" she said, once she'd swallowed.

Jen sighed. "What happened? I thought you two were having such a good night."

"We did have a good night," Agatha said. "Not all good nights have to end in sex, you know? Unlike some people, I don't climb into bed on the first date."

"So it was a date!" Jen exclaimed, pointing a finger into Agatha's face.

Agatha rolled her eyes and slapped the hand away.

"Didn't your mother ever teach you that it's rude to put your fingers in somebody else's face — DON'T." Jen gave her a wicked grin, but she just shrugged and sipped her coffee. "And it wasn't a date…at least, I don't think so."

"What makes you uncertain?" Jen asked, seeming genuinely curious. She tilted her head in a way that reminded Agatha of Rio. Her eyes flicked to her phone screen again, but there were no new messages since the last time she checked the phone (two full minutes ago).

"For one, I sat with you, your date, and Rio's kid sister, who also happens to be the artist whose photograph I bought just last weekend before even meeting the subject of that photograph, who happened to be the woman onstage with whom I may or may not have been on a date."

"So…it's complicated," Jen said, after a long moment of contemplation. "Life is complicated sometimes, Agatha. So is dating." She took another sip of her coffee and reached past Agatha, placing her empty cup on her bedside table, then she settled in next to her, slipping under the sheets in her bougie hoodie and matching sweatpants. Thankfully, she wasn't wearing shoes, at least. "We were complicated once, too."

"I remember," Agatha said. "And now we're sisters. I don't want Rio to be my sister." She placed her half-empty cup next to Jen's and leaned back against the headboard.

"What do you want her to be then?" Jen asked. Agatha could see her grin in the peripheral of her vision.

"Less annoying than you," Agatha huffed in return. "Which she's already accomplished so far, so that's a plus."

"Fuck off," Jen snorted. She was silent for a moment. "Seriously, though," she said. "It's obvious you like her. And that she likes you. You two just have to stop being useless lesbians and admit it to each other."

Agatha elbowed her in the ribs, but she didn't say anything as she took another sip of her drink, thinking…

"We kissed," she said, finally. "Well, I kissed her."

Jen's eyes were seconds away from popping out of her skull and rolling around on Agatha's clean purple sheets. "What?!" she squeaked. "When?!"

"Last night," Agatha said. "I walked her to her door and…Dulce came out. She nearly knocked us both over in her rush to get to your apartment." She furrowed her brow. "Wait, weren't you meant to be helping her today? Why are you here?"

"She and Morgan were canoodling on the roof when I checked in on them, like, an hour ago. She's fine. Finish the damn story." Jen was leaning in, fully engaged.

Agatha snorted, rolling her eyes. "She told us where she was going and left," Agatha said. "Then I met Rio's cats."

"You went inside the apartment?" Jen asked, practically squealing.

"No," Agatha said. "I didn't get that far. Her cats came out, and I petted them, but I didn't actually go into the apartment. My car was idling on the street, so I couldn't really stay. I just stood up, said goodbye, and I was heading toward the door when I just had this…thought."

Agatha remembered it clear as day, as though it happened just moments ago instead of nearly twelve hours ago now.

She had taken no more than three steps in the direction of the sliding electric doors in the lobby. She could see her hazards still flashing just outside, knew that she'd get a ticket if she let her car sit there for too long since it wasn't a parking spot. But there was something keeping her from moving forward. It felt like she was forgetting something, but her pizza was in the car. Her car keys were hanging off the carabiner on her belt loop. Her house keys too. Her phone was in her pocket and her cardigan was on her body. She wasn't really forgetting anything.

But she was.

She turned around to see Rio start to hobble into the apartment, heard her chuckle as she admonished Swan for being dramatic about something, saw the curve her cheeks as she smiled and…Agatha didn't actively make the decision to turn and reach for her. It was as though her body was making the decision for her. Her hand had reached out for Rio's elbow before she could even blink and then her face was coming at her and all Agatha could do was press her lips to Rio's.

By the time her brain caught up, her tongue had swiped out against Rio's bottom lip and she felt the vibration of Rio's moan against her mouth.

That might have been what snapped her out of whatever trance she was in and made her pull back (several steps, mind you) from the other woman until her back hit the opposite wall and she just stared, wide-eyed, at Rio for several seconds, breathing hard like she'd run a mile.

Jen was staring as Agatha explained all of this.

"And then what?" she demanded, leaning in with wide eyes.

"Then I…thanked her for the pizza," Agatha said. "And I left."

Jen's eye twitched.

"You fucking idiot," she murmured.

Agatha groaned, dragging the comforter over her head. "I know," she said.

"You absolute imbecile," Jen admonished, grabbing a pillow and hitting her over the head with it. "I ought to smother you and put you out of your misery, but that would be too kind."

"Okay, that's a little much," Agatha said, popping her head back out from the comforter. Jen hit her full in the face with the pillow. "Rude."

"Girl!" Jen huffed, hitting her again. "Why," hit, "would," hit, "you," hit, hit, hit, "walk away!?" Another hit. "You absolute buffoon!"

"I didn't even mean to kiss her!" Agatha argued back, ripping the pillow from Jen's grip.

"Then what did you mean to do, dumbass?" Jen huffed. "You literally took every step to initiate the kiss!"

"I wasn't in control of my body," Agatha grumbled, crossing her arms over her chest.

"That's even worse!" Jen exclaimed, throwing her hands up. "That means that you were acting on instinct and then you actively fought against that instinct even though it's what both of you wanted!"

"I don't know that it's what she wanted," Agatha argued.

"Girl." Jen's face was more serious than Agatha had seen it in a long time. She leveled at her with those big brown eyes of hers. "You deserve good things, Agatha. And, according to Alice, Rio is a very good thing. And she likes you. Let yourself have that."

Agatha's heart clenched in her chest and her shoulders dropped. "It's not a good time, Jen. I just…I just got diagnosed with a serious medical condition."

"One that Rio has, too," Jen pointed out.

"Exactly!" Agatha exclaimed. "And she walks with a cane!"

"Don't tell me you're gonna be ableist right now, bitch. I thought you were better than that!"

"No! Oh my God…" Agatha groaned, pressing the pillow over her head. "No, of course I'm not being…I don't care about the cane, okay? If I were perfectly healthy, I wouldn't really think anything of it. I'd probably find it hot."

"Freak," Jen muttered.

"Make up your mind!" Agatha shoved Jen's shoulder. "Look, the cane is not the reason I'm second-guessing myself, I don't think. It's…well, okay, maybe it's the thought that, one day, that could be me. I could need a cane someday."

"So?" Jen huffed. "Then you'd be two bad bitches with canes. So what?"

"So…" Agatha shook her head. "Jen, I'm a runner. Not just recreationally. I don't do relationships. You know that."

"Too well," Jen scoffed. "You're only twenty-nine, Agatha."

"So are you," Agatha retorted. "And you don't have to deal with the bullshit that I do. I have a chronic illness now. It's a lot of baggage to carry into a relationship."

"Every bad bitch has baggage," Jen said. "Doesn't mean we should have to carry it all ourselves or avoid living our lives to the fullest."

"Thanks, Gandhi," Agatha replied, patting her knee.

"Asshole," Jen muttered, but she couldn't fight her grin as she shook her head. "Seriously, though. You're not the only one with baggage. Hell, you'd be hard-pressed to find anybody our age without it. Stop worrying so much and just…go for it. It'll be worth it."

"Once again, I don't do relationships," Agatha reiterated.

"Just because you haven't doesn't mean you can't," Jen said. "You might surprise yourself."

Agatha was quiet for a long moment at that.

"What if I hurt her?" she asked after a long moment of silence.

"She's a big girl," Jen replied. "She'll be fine." She nudged Agatha's shoulder. "And look at you, thinking about the feelings of others. Where was that concern for me when you stole my hoodie?"

"Would you let that go?" Agatha groaned. "You got it back!"

"After a year!" Jen grumbled, reaching for another pillow to hit her with. "You didn't care about my feelings about it!"

"It wasn't even a nice hoodie!" Agatha snorted. "Not like these bougie, Egyptian cotton hoodies or whatever you've got now." She tugged on the sleeve of Jen's current hoodie, which was buttery soft and smooth.

Hmm, she might just need to steal this one from her closet later.

"It was so!" Jen argued, then grunted. "Not important. Point is, you have got to stop thinking about how it could go wrong and think about how it could go right."

"When did you become a fortune cookie?"

"Stop deflecting, Agatha," Jen said, her voice dead serious again. "Rio likes you. You like her. Just…give it a shot. What's the worst that could happen?" Agatha opened her mouth, but Jen placed her hand over it before a single syllable could eek out. "Rhetorical," she said. "You're both grown, adult women. You both like each other and have more or less been pursuing…something for the last week. Just…go for it."

"But—"

"No more buts," Jen said. "You've already created this whole list of things that could go wrong in your own head. What about all the things that could go right?"

"Like what?" Agatha huffed. "We fall in love and have our happily ever after?" she mocked. "That's a fantasy. And we've only known each other a week!"

"And the chemistry is pure fire," Jen pointed out. "Trust me: I have a PhD in chemistry." Agatha rolled her eyes and nudged Jen as she cackled. "You don't have to jump into anything with her, okay? Take it slow if you must. Rio doesn't exactly strike me as the kind of person who'd try to force you into anything you don't want."

"Because you know her so well?" Agatha snorted.

"Alice literally won't shut up about her," Jen said. "I was a little jealous for a minute, but when I asked if she had ever thought about hooking up with her, she literally gagged at the thought." Jen snorted. "God, she's so cute."

"How are you this into a girl you've known less than three days?" Agatha asked.

"Look, you may not be a U-Hauler, but I certainly am," Jen said. "I'm ready to risk it all for her. I've already started planning our prenup."

"How romantic," Agatha snorted.

"I know, right?" Jen said, wiggling her brows. "If things don't work out with Alice, I'll be really, really sad, but I'll get over it. I know she will, too. But she's worth the risk." She took a deep breath. "You can decide for yourself if Rio is worth the risk, too. I'm not going to push you into doing anything you truly do not want to do, but don't talk yourself out of something that you do want just because it might not turn out perfectly. That's dumb. And you're a lot of things, Agatha Harkness, but you're not dumb."

"Not sure if I should actually take that as a compliment," Agatha said. "What things am I, exactly?"

"Annoying, for one," Jen retorted. "Stubborn, thick-headed, bitchy, emotionally-constipated…"

"Okay, fuck you," Agatha huffed, shoving her away.

Jen laughed, reaching with her freakishly long arms to wrap them around Agatha, pulling her into a hug that the shorter woman immediately tried to worm out of.

"But you're also protective of the ones you love, which I know includes me now." She gave Agatha a cheesy grin. "And you're naturally kind, as hard you fight against that instinct."

"Take that back!" Agatha growled.

"Never," Jen snorted. "And you are loyal—"

"Loyalty is for dogs," Agatha huffed. Jen ignored her.

"And you're creative and smart and hard-working and you're really bad at taking compliments even though you pretend to be full of yourself."

"Fuck you, I'm exceptional," Agatha huffed, still attempting to shove Jen away, but the other woman had a vice-like grip on her.

"I know you are," Jen said, hugging Agatha more tightly. "But I also know that you don't actually believe that."

"Yes I do," Agatha insisted.

"No you don't," Jen snorted. "But that's fine. It's true whether you believe it or not."

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she stopped fighting Jen's hold on her.

"One day, I hope you will actually believe it, though," Jen said. "I hope you'll stop fighting against it and let yourself have the things that I know you deserve. I hope you'll eventually know that you deserve them, too."

"I'm guessing Rio is one of those things?" Agatha murmured against Jen's collarbone.

"She could be," Jen affirmed, "if you would just stop being an idiot."

"You just said I wasn't an idiot!" Agatha argued.

"I said you're not dumb," Jen said. "You can still be an idiot even if you're not dumb."

"I hate you."

"You love me."

Agatha hated that she was right. Again.

Jennifer Kale being right should be a crime.

They sat there in the bed for a long time before Agatha pulled away. Thankfully, Jen let her go this time, watching her as she reached for her phone and unlocked it.

"Who are you calling?" she asked.

"Nobody," Agatha retorted, tapping at her phone's screen. "I'm texting Rio."

She couldn't see it from the corner of her eye, but she just knew that Jen was giving her that smug smile of hers that Agatha absolutely hated. Bitch.

Agatha (12:24): Hey, how'd you sleep?

Rio💀🌺 (12:24): Like the dead. You?

Well, that was quick, Agatha thought with a soft grin. It was as though Rio had been staring at her phone, waiting for her text.

Had Agatha said she was going to text? Or did Rio expect it because of the barely-there kiss? Why hadn't Rio just texted her?

"Don't overthink it," Jen murmured from beside her, looking down at her own phone. "Just text."

Agatha frowned at her. "I wasn't—"

"Girl, I can hear the gears whirring in your brain," Jen said. "Just chill. Be cool."

"I'm plenty cool," Agatha huffed, looking back down at her phone. She still hadn't answered Rio. "Um, what would a cool person say to this question?" she asked, showing Jen the text.

"Um, the truth?" Jen asked, shrugging. "It's a pretty straightforward question."

"Right," Agatha said, flushing.

Agatha (12:27): I slept alright.

"Lame," Jen snorted when Agatha showed her the response after she'd sent it.

"You said to be honest!"

"Honest, not boring."

"You're the worst."

Rio💀🌺 (12:29): That's cool.

Rio💀🌺 (12:30): Did you burn that monstrosity from last night?

Agatha snorted, rolling her eyes. Jen peered over her shoulder.

"What 'monstrosity'?" she asked.

"My Hawaiian pizza," Agatha laughed, shaking her head.

"Heathen."

"You put spinach on your pizza," Agatha huffed. "Don't even talk."

"It tastes good!" Jen defended.

"So does pineapple!"

"Lies!"

Agatha rolled her eyes and tapped out a response.

Agatha (12:32): I was actually planning on having it for lunch

Agatha (12:33): w/some fava beans and a nice chianthi

Rio💀🌺 (12:34): fitting for a psychopath

Rio💀🌺 (12:35): what plans do you have for the rest of the day?

Agatha felt her face warm at that. She could feel Jen's smile over her shoulder, and she did her best to ignore it as she tried to formulate a response.

"Just be honest," Jen sung in her ear. Agatha swatted at her like she was a fly, hitting her in the cheek.

Agatha bit her lip as she stared at the empty text box on her phone, the blinking line waiting for her to type something, the keyboard…

Agatha (12:38): Depends…what did you have in mind?

"Thattagirl," Jen said, patting her on the shoulder.

"Shut up," Agatha grumbled as she watched the three little dots do the wave on her screen. Her heart was thumping a pattern against her ribcage as she waited for the words to appear on the screen.

Rio💀🌺 (12:40): How do you feel about gardening?

Agatha's eyes widened at that, and she showed Jen the text.

Jen's eyebrows rose at that.

"Does she know you kill every plant you touch?"

She received a swift punch to the ribs for that.

Agatha (12:42): I'm like the Grim Reaper when it comes to gardening

Agatha (12:42): but for flowers

Rio💀🌺 (12:43): good thing I'm not working w/flowers today

Rio💀🌺 (12:43): and it's not so much gardening as harvesting

Rio💀🌺 (12:44): usually I use alice as my free labor

Rio💀🌺 (12:44): but she's at rehearsal so…

Agatha (12:45): who said my labor is free?

Rio💀🌺 (12:45): I'm sure we can come to an agreement on compensation

"Ooh," Jen said into her ear. "Like kisses?" She made kissy noises that made Agatha want to punch her right in the mouth.

She settled for flicking her between the eyes. Jen shoved her, pouting as she rubbed the affected spot on her forehead. Agatha snickered.

Agatha (12:46): like more hawaiian pizza?

Rio💀🌺 (12:46): okay 1) that shit is canadian, not hawaiian

Rio💀🌺 (12:47): 2) I can think of something better as payment

"So she is going to pay you in kisses!" Jen exclaimed.

"Will you go home!" Agatha huffed. "And stopped snooping, nosy!"

"Ugh," Jen huffed. "There's nothing to do at home!"

Agatha narrowed her eyes at Jen, then a thought came to her and she grinned, turning back to her phone.

Agatha (12:48): Mind if I bring an extra set of hands with me to help?

Rio💀🌺 (12:48): The more the merrier!

Agatha (12:49): Great! Just let me know when and where we should meet you!

Rio sent a thumbs up and then a location and time a few moments later while Agatha was padding around her room, looking for garden-appropriate clothing. She found an old pair of paint-splattered overalls and a pair of thick leather boots in the back of her closet.

Jen watched her, brows furrowed.

"I'm not going," she said.

"Yes, you are," Agatha responded, simply, like it was a fact of life.

"I don't do dirt, Agatha," Jen huffed, crossing her arms over her chest.

"I've seen you take baths in mud, Jennifer," Agatha retorted.

"That's different!" Jen exclaimed. "That mud was healing!"

"This dirt could be healing, as well," Agatha shot back. "And it's organic!"

"We don't know that," Jen grumbled.

"You think Rio manufactures her own dirt?" Agatha scoffed.

"I don't know her life," Jen muttered.

"Come on, Jen," Agatha said. "You just said that there was nothing to do at home. Now you have something to do while you wait for your dinner date with Alice!"

"But I'm gonna get dirty," Jen practically moaned.

"Good thing man invented showers," Agatha shot back, tossing her an old tee and a pair of jeans for Jen to borrow. They'd be a little short and probably loose in the hips, but Agatha also had belts.

"You expect me to believe that men invented showers?" Jen snorted. "Not a chance." She wrinkled her nose at the jeans. "No way," she said. "I'm not going."

She tossed them down onto Agatha's bed like that was the final say.

Forty minutes later, she sat grumpily in the passenger seat of Agatha's car as they made their way up the driveway of some small farm in a more rural part of New Jersey. Jen was wearing Agatha's jeans, which, as predicted, stopped just before her ankles, and a pair of Agatha's boots, which miraculously fit her just fine with a bare of thick socks on her feet. She also wore one of Agatha's faded hoodies over the tee she borrowed.

"I hate you," Jen grumbled, not for the first time, as Agatha pulled up behind a pickup truck, sending off a quick text to Rio to let her know that they had arrived at the address she'd sent her.

"You love me," Agatha snorted, slipping out of the car. "Now get out."

Jen growled at her, but she did end up getting out of the orange SUV. She looked like a petulant child with her pouty lips and furrowed brows.

"Hey," Agatha said, "this was your idea, remember? I would have happily stayed in bed all day had you not needled me into texting Rio."

"Me and my big mouth," Jen huffed, stomping after Agatha as she made her way toward the front door of the modestly-sized house next to a fenced-in pumpkin patch.

Before Agatha could make it all the way up the path to the door, it opened and Rio stepped out, wearing a pair of overalls not too unlike the ones Agatha had put on, only hers were green and far more worn in the knees. She wore a long-sleeve thermal shirt underneath them. Her cane was held securely in her right hand. She grinned when she locked eyes with Agatha.

Agatha's entire face went warm when she remembered the sensation of those lips against hers from the night before.

Rio's grin flickered when she saw Jen coming up behind her, but it didn't drop entirely.

"When you said you were bringing an extra set of hands," Rio said, "I did not think you meant Jen."

"I've been kidnapped," Jen said. "Call the police."

"Stop being dramatic," Agatha huffed. "She's just trying to kill time before her date with Alice tonight, so I figured we could put her to work."

"I better get proper compensation for this," Jen said, glaring at Agatha.

Agatha waved her off, keeping her eyes on Rio. "So," she said, "what, exactly, are we harvesting?"

"Nothing too crazy," Rio said. "Just some pumpkins." She motioned toward the pumpkin patch, which was far smaller than the one that Gran had taken her to every fall as a child to pick a pumpkin for them to carve together for their front yard. This one looked like it had been started almost by accident, but kept going out of habit or something.

"Those look heavy, Agatha!" Jen whined in her ear. Agatha elbowed her away.

"Did you grow those?" she asked Rio.

"Not by myself," Rio answered, turning to admire the small patch of pumpkins. "I'm more of a helper, to be honest. This is all Tio's doing."

"Tio?" Agatha asked. "I thought you said you didn't have any uncles."

"Oh, he's not my uncle," Rio said. "He's the guy that I used to work for at the flower shop. His nieces and nephews used to have part-time jobs there, too, so he just came to be known as Tio. His real name is Jesús."

"Why aren't his nieces and nephews helping him then?" Jen grumbled.

Agatha elbowed her again and gave her a look.

"Because it's my turn," Rio chuckled. "I volunteered to take pumpkin duty this year. I didn't expect them to get quite that big though." She frowned looking at the plump pumpkins. "Chuché and Lupe are on their way to help, too, though."

"Who?" Agatha asked, blinking at her.

"Tio's nephew and grand-niece," Rio informed her with a soft smile. "Chuché will do most of the heavy lifting. We just need to cut the vines and plant the seeds for the next bath. Lupe likes that part."

"And where, exactly, are we taking these pumpkins?" Agatha asked.

"Just loading them into Tio's pickup truck," Rio said, motioning to the truck parked in front of Agatha's car. "He's gonna sell them at a farmer's market in town tomorrow with his nieces."

"Not gonna make much of a profit, is he?" Jen commented. Agatha glared at her. "What?" she said, holding up her hands. "I've seen farmers come in with hundreds of pumpkins at those markets. That's, like, three dozen at most."

"His main income comes from his flower shop," Rio explained. "The pumpkins are just a kind of yearly side hustle. Maybe semi-annual, if the weather's right for it. He didn't even mean to start growing the pumpkins. They just happened."

"How do pumpkin patches just happen?" Agatha asked as they started walking to said patch.

"Your wife's idiot nephew gets drunk on too many ales one October night, eats about a pound of the pumpkin seeds you were planning on roasting, and then pukes on the land where you were previously growing tomatoes," Rio explained with a grin. "Tio thought he'd discovered a new kind of tomato when they started growing a few months later. Now, he just grows them all year round. Replanted the tomatoes elsewhere, too."

Jen's estimate of three dozen was right on the money, it seemed. There were just under forty pumpkins, of various shapes and sizes. All of them were bright orange with dark green stems, all perfectly ripe and ready to be cut from the vines.

"These look fantastic," Jen said. "Like a painting. That color is so vibrant." She slipped her phone from her pocket. "Mind if I take a picture? I've been looking for some autumn inspiration for my art."

Rio shrugged. "Go ahead," she said.

Jen immediately started taking pictures.

"Why would you volunteer to do this?" Agatha asked, quietly. "I mean, it's gotta be hard with the…" she motioned to Rio's cane.

"Picking up the heavier ones is, yeah," Rio admitted. "But Tio helps me with that for the most part. This year, he hurt his back, which is where Chuché and Lupe come in. Besides that, there's not much anybody else can do that I can't. Even with the cane."

Agatha absorbed that for a moment, before nodding. "Yeah," she said, "of course. Sorry."

"Nothing to apologize for," Rio assured her. "It's a pretty common assumption."

"Still, I shouldn't just assume that—"

"Look who's here," Rio interrupted, looking past Agatha's shoulder and hobbling a few steps around her. "Lupe!"

"Rio!" a high voice squealed. Agatha turned just as a blur of red slammed against Rio's front, nearly knocking her over. Agatha reached out as if to catch her, but Rio caught herself on her good leg and her cane, wrapping her arm around a slightly shorter body.

"¿Cómo estás?" Rio laughed into a pile of red curls.

"Bien!" the little body squeaked. "Te he extrañado mucho!"

"Yo Tambien, baby girl," Rio replied, pulling back. "How's your mom? And your brothers?"

"Luis is annoying, as always," the little girl said in English. "And Pedro is always grumpy now. Mami says he's going through," she lowered her voice and leaned in, "puberty."

Agatha couldn't help herself as she snorted out a laugh, alerting the girl to her presence. She had the biggest, roundest, greenest eyes that Agatha had ever seen, her face a constellation of freckles. Her cheeks turned pink and she went somewhat shy, pressing herself to Rio's front. Rio placed her hands on her shoulders.

"Lupe," she said, "this is Agatha and Jen, my friends from Westview. They're going to help us with the cutting and planting today."

"Hola," Lupe mumbled. "Cómo están?"

"Estoy bien," Agatha answered with a kind smile, holding out her hand. "¿Y tú?"

"¿La gringa habla español?" Lupe asked, looking up at Rio, who snorted and poked her in the side, eliciting a giggle.

"Don't call her that, jerk," she said, offering Agatha an apologetic smile.

Lupe's giggles were a little mischievous, as was the glint in her eyes, but she was still pretty shy. Still, she reached out to shake Agatha's outstretched hand. Then Jen's.

"Ooh, I love your hair," Jen said. "It's so gorgeous and curly."

"Thanks!" Lupe said, reaching up to play with the bright red curls sticking out of her ponytail. "I like your…" Her eyes went wide when she realized that Jen was bald. "…sweater. It looks soft."

Agatha had to bite her lip to keep from laughing out loud at the way Jen's face flickered though the taller woman's bright smile never dropped, to her credit.

"Thanks," Jen said, her voice a little strangled.

"Okay!" a booming voice came from behind them. Agatha turned to see a man with dark curly hair graying at the roots come up behind them. He had a wide grin and broad shoulders. He was a giant of a man with a kind face. "Let's get started, shall we?" His voice was deep and thick with an accent. He smiled at Jen and Agatha, both of whom were dwarfed by his immense height. "Hello, señoritas," he said. "I'm Chuché. Nice to meet you both."

"Jen," Jen said, shaking his hand.

"Agatha," Agatha said, doing the same.

Something in his eyes flickered at that, and he glanced at Rio with a small smile, but said nothing.

"Okay," he said, "now that we all know each other, let's get to pumpkin smashing."

"Pumpkin picking, papi," Lupe sighed, rolling her eyes.

"Isn't that what I said?" Chuché said, winking at Agatha.

Lupe rolled her eyes, looking at Rio. "Men," she huffed, before stomping off toward the pumpkin patch."

"I like her," Jen said, grinning at Rio as she followed after the little girl.

Agatha rolled her eyes as she snorted, but she didn't miss the little grin that Rio sent her way — or the subsequent glare she sent Chuché when he bumped her shoulder as they started their own walk toward the pumpkin patch.

Chapter End Notes

Comments would be great.

Also I want it to be noted that:

a) I do not like Hawaiian pizza. I'm sorry if anybody is insulted by that. I will not adjust my morals.
b) I do like spinach on pizza. spinach is delicious. I will not compromise on that.

Also, if anybody from a spanish-speaking country can tell me WHY the nickname for Jesus is some form of Chuch, that would also be amazing because I cannot figure it out and the person who is named that in my family doesn't even know! Thanks

Chapter 12: Pumpkin &amp; Spice

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Rio get a little bit closer. There's pumpkins and spicy things (not that kind, sorry).

Chapter Notes

:)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twelve

If Agatha never saw another pumpkin for as long as she lived, she’d be alright with that. She’d never particularly been a fan of pumpkins, anyway, but she was even less of a fan after having to heft them across the tiny patch and into the bed of Tio’s pickup truck.

Her back felt like a slinky as she carried the last pumpkin across the gravel driveway and plopped it down on the pile. She bent at the waist next to the truck, groaning at the aches and pains that vibrated down her spine. She could physically feel the myelin peeling away from her spine, both due to her MS and the work she’d just spent the last two hours doing.

She needed to lie down. Preferably on a bed or a couch, but she wouldn’t actually be all that opposed to the gravel, so long as she were horizontal. She could make it work.

“You’re so dramatic,” Jen snorted, sidling up next to her.

“You have no room to talk,” Agatha huffed, glaring at her through the lock of sweaty hair that had fallen out of her ponytail and now kept getting in the way of her vision. “I saw the tears in your eyes when you chipped a nail.”

“It hurt,” Jen muttered, looking at the offending pointer finger, which had an ugly-shaped chip taken out of it. “And these were expensive.”

“Cry me a river,” Agatha huffed, red-faced and sweaty. “You barely did any work.”

“I helped Rio cut the vines!” Jen pointed out. “It’s not my fault you opted for carrying the pumpkins instead of cutting them with us.”

“It would have taken a lot longer to lug the damn things to the truck if Chuché was doing it all by himself,” Agatha said. “I didn’t think walking back and forth twenty feet would be so tiring.” She straightened up, groaning at the twinge in her lower back, and took a deep breath.

“Well, look at the bright side,” Jen said, leaning up against the truck next to her: “at least you got a workout today. And,” she lowered her voice, “you got to see Rio get all sweaty, too.” She waggled her eyebrows, suggestively.

“There’s something wrong with you,” Agatha said. “Psychologically.”

“At least I’m not a pussy when it comes to my feelings,” Jen retorted. “And I actually have a date tonight, so” she stuck out her tongue to punctuate her sentence.

“Does Alice know that she’s dating a toddler?” Agatha snorted.

“Heads up!”

Agatha and Jen both turned toward the voice just as a water bottle flew right by Jen’s shoulder and the taller woman squeaked, falling to the floor in surprise.

“Sorry!” Chuché called, but that didn’t stop him from throwing a second bottle – more gently this time – in Agatha’s direction. She caught it with a surprising amount of ease and nodded back to him in thanks before unscrewing the lid and downing a quarter of it in three deep gulps.

“The hell is wrong with you?” she heard Rio huff, but there was laughter in her voice as she hobbled toward them. Agatha looked up to see Chuché rubbing his arm with an exaggerated pout while a dirt-covered Lupe shook her hand at him with her hands on her hips. Rio caught her gaze and rolled her eyes with a little lopsided smirk, and Agatha’s heart did a stupid little cartoony skip. “Sorry about him,” Rio said. “He grew up around a lot of guys who could take a water bottle to the head.”

“You callin’ us hard-headed?” Chuché huffed, playfully.

“Very,” Lupe said before Rio could even respond. Rio snorted and held up her hand. Lupe ran to slap it, giggling as her father’s jaw dropped in mock outrage.

“You’re grounded,” he huffed.

“No, I’m not,” Lupe retorted, confidently, her hands on her hips, her dirt-streaked ginger hair falling out of her ponytail like springs. 

Chuché didn’t even try to argue with her, just pouting at his daughter. Lupe rolled her eyes and ran at him, throwing her arms around his waist. His pout turned into a smile as he chuckled, brushing a kiss to her forehead as he squeezed her tightly, lifting her up and spinning her around as she squealed.

Agatha watched them, her chest aching a little bit, her eyes burning. She forced herself to look away, clearing her throat as she tucked a lock of hair behind her ear. 

“So,” she said, “anything else we need to do?” She looked back at Rio, who was already facing her, an odd look on her face. 

“Yeah,” Rio said, after a second of just continuing to watch Agatha. “Yeah. We just need to plant the new seeds. That’s usually Lupe’s job.” She smiled down at the girl, whose father had placed her down on the ground. 

Lupe reached into her pocket and pulled out a couple packets of pumpkin seeds, grinning through the dirt on her face. “It’s the best part!” she told them.

“You need help?” Jen asked, nearly knocking Agatha on her ass in shock. 

“You’re offering to help with planting seeds?” Agatha asked, eyes wide. 

“I’m a helpful person,” Jen huffed, crossing her arms. 

“Since when?”

“Listen, bitch–”

“Language,” Chuché and Lupe said in unison.

“Please!” Rio snorted, looking at the former. “I’ve heard you say way worse in front of your toddler.”

“Lie! Don’t listen to her, Lupita…and don’t tell your mother.”

Lupe rolled her eyes again, but then she grabbed Jen’s hand and started tugging her in the direction of the now mostly bare patch of soil. “You can help,” she said, “but you have to do everything I say.”

“Yes, Ma’am,” Jen said, smiling affectionately down at the girl. “You’re the boss.”

“And she knows it,” Chuché muttered under his breath, but when Agatha looked at him his eyes were shining with affection, a little grin on his lips.

Her chest ached again and she swallowed thickly, looking back to Rio. 

“She’s cute,” she said. “And bossy.”

Rio snorted. “Yeah,” she said. “She definitely gets that from her mother.”

“Oh, without a doubt,” Chuché said.

“I’m telling her you said that,” Rio said, placing her hand on Agatha’s back. As Chuché spluttered after her, she guided Agatha toward the porch. “Come on,” she said. “Let’s get something to eat. I think Tio made guacamole and tostadas.”

“What are tostadas?” Agatha asked, trying to ignore the heat that sprouted from Rio’s hand.

“Tortilla chips,” Rio informed her. “Homemade. Tio’s a great cook. His guac is a little spicy, though. I hope you don’t mind.”

“I’m okay with a little spice,” Agatha retorted, and it may have sounded a bit flirtatious. But that was a total accident. Honestly. That doesn’t mean she didn’t feel a slight thrill at the way Rio’s cheeks went just slightly pinker (from what Agatha could see under the dirt she’d wiped there, anyway).

“Well, it’s not just a little,” Rio warned. “He’s Mexican. He likes his spice. It can really get intense.”

“I can handle it,” Agatha assured her as they stepped through the screen door straight into a large living space. The house had an open floor plan, with the kitchen visible from the front door. There was a man hobbling around, slightly bent over as he shuffled around the kitchen, grabbing ingredients to toss into three separate bowls. 

He looked up when they entered.

“You’re done already?” he asked. 

“Chuché pulled his weight this time,” Rio said.

“Hey!” a voice called from the other side of the screen door. 

Rio snickered as she hobbled inside, leaning heavily on her cane. She was favoring her good leg more than usual now, but she didn’t show any signs of pain otherwise. Agatha still glanced at her from time to time as she led her to the kitchen island, Rio’s hand still a welcome weight on the small of her back. Her touch was warm and a little bit electric, sending shivers up Agatha’s spine.

She mourned the loss of Rio’s electric fingers when they reached the sink, their elbows knocking together as they washed as much dirt as possible off of their hands. Then, the other woman perched herself on a stool at the island, in front of the three bowls of guacamole and an even bigger bowl of chips. She motioned for Agatha to claim the stool next to her, which she did with a shy smile.

“Wow,” Agatha said, eyeing the food. “That is a lot of guacamole.”

“I have to make three different batches,” Tio informed her, “to account for different tastes.” He pointed to the red bowl. “This one has serrano peppers; it is the spiciest.” He pointed to the blue bowl. “This one has jalapeños; it’s mild. Very good.” He pointed to the green bowl just in front of Rio. “That one is Rio’s guacamole: it is not spicy.”

Agatha turned to look at Rio, who avoided her gaze as she plucked a chip and dipped it into the green bowl of guacamole. She was blushing again.

Agatha felt the taunt rising in her throat, but she swallowed it back as she reached for a chip of her own, dipping it into the blue bowl.

“Ah,” Tio said, “a mild girl.” He nodded. “That’s alright. Not everybody can handle serranos…or any spice at all.” He glanced pointedly at Rio, who glared back at him. He snickered.

“I just wanted to see how spicy you consider mild to be,” Agatha said. “I happen to love spicy food, but it’s definitely an acquired tolerance.”

She took a bite of the chip and hummed. This was really good guacamole. The avocados tasted perfectly ripe and there was a good balance in the onions, tomatoes, and cilantro. It had just the right amount of saltiness, too. 

“One that Rio has not acquired.”

“Okay, Tio,” Rio huffed. “Not all of us were bottle fed hot sauce as an infant. Just because I don’t like your spicy ass peppers doesn’t mean I can’t take it.”

“Prove it then,” Tio said, plucking up the red bowl and placing it in front of Rio. “Take a bite.”

Rio blanched, looking at the bowl, then up at Tio. Then, for some reason, she cast a glance at Agatha, who just took another bite of her own chip, munching slowly as she watched the exchange.

Rio turned back to Tio and glared at him before picking up a chip and dipping it into the red bowl, scooping up a small amount at first.

“Ah!” Tio scoffed, shaking his head. He said nothing more, but that single noise was very condescending. And challenging.

Rio accepted the challenge by dipping her chip again, piling it with the guacamole until it crackled, straining under the weight of all the ingredients. A large chunk of red serrano pepper was submerged halfway into the green mixture. Agatha’s eyes widened at it, wondering if Rio saw it as well.

If she did, she made no move to flick it off the chip – that would have been admitting weakness. The staring contest she was currently having with Tio left no room for weakness. She stared that man directly in the eye as she brought the chip to her lips. Tio stared back, a glimmer of mirth in his eyes and in the sideways quirk of his lips. 

Rio’s hand hesitated a bit before reaching her lips, her eyes flicking down to stare at the single bit of pepper atop the small mountain of green. Agatha heard her take a deep breath in through her nose before her lips parted and she shoved the entire chip into her mouth.

Tio and Agatha watched her chew for a long moment. Rio continued to glare at him as she chewed slowly and then swallowed, clearing her throat. Agatha didn’t miss the beads of sweat that formed at her hairline, but Rio didn’t blink or move to swipe them away, obviously trying to prove a point even as her cheeks reddened and a tear formed at the corner of her eye.

Agatha reached for another chip and dipped it into the red bowl, which snapped both Rio’s and Tio’s attention toward her. She offered them a small smile as she casually brought the chip to her lips and, like Rio, ate the whole thing in one bite.

Tio’s big bushy gray eyebrows reached to his receding hairline, his hazel eyes widening in shock and awe as Agatha chewed and swallowed.

“Not bad,” she said. “A little bit spicy, but pretty good, nonetheless.”

Tio’s jaw dropped and he spluttered for a moment. “A little bit?!?!?” he exclaimed. “What do you mean a little bit?!?!”

Agatha shrugged. “I’ve had spicier,” she said.

It wasn’t a lie. She’d been a fan of spicy food throughout high school and college. Gran couldn’t have much in the way of spice, but Agatha’s ‘rebellious’ face involved her pouring way too much hot sauce on everything she ate for a long time. Now, as an adult woman with a fully-formed prefrontal cortex, she had no idea what the purpose of that was. She wasn’t actually rebelling (Gran didn’t give a shit how spicy her food was so long as she didn’t force her to eat it) and she’d given herself a number of stomachaches as she adapted to the spice. 

Now, at least, she could tolerate a certain level of spice. Like serrano peppers, which were spicier than jalapeños (which Agatha enjoyed from time to time) but not by that much. 

Rio looked like she was dying inside, though, even as she stared in shock at Agatha, who licked the remnants of the spicy guacamole from her lips. Her cheeks went even redder if that was possible. Agatha just smirked, looking between her and Tio, who looked like he was still fuming that the gringa called his spiciest guac “just a little spicy” which seemed to have initiated a hard reset in the man’s brain. 

He started muttering something in Spanish as he huffed out of the room, shaking his head and casting glances back at Agatha as he disappeared down the hall. A door clicked shut a moment later.

“Want milk or something?” Agatha asked, grinning at Rio, who was still sweating. Her nose had also started to run and there were tears gathering at the corners of both eyes, escaping and running down her cheeks.

“Yes, please,” Rio croaked, fanning at her mouth. “Or sour cream. Whatever you can find in the fridge.” She motioned toward the fridge and Agatha jumped up, practically skipping to the fridge to grab whatever dairy product she could find to ease the burn.

There was no sour cream, but there was a half-empty gallon of milk on the top shelf, which she grabbed. She was about to ask Rio where the cups were when the gallon was torn from her hands. Agatha’s eyes widened as she watched Rio desperately unscrew the top and place her mouth right over the top, then tip her head back to chug as much of the milk as possible, tears streaming down her cheeks still. 

“Okay,” Agatha said, after Rio had definitely drunk enough. She placed her hands on the now nearly-empty container of milk. “That’s enough,” she said, helping Rio to lower it and remove it from her mouth. “You’re going to puke if you keep going.”

“Will that make the burning stop?” Rio asked, sniffling as her nose continued to run.

“It might make it worse,” Agatha informed her, handing her a paper towel, “considering the contents of your stomach right now.”

Rio whimpered. “I had spicy food,” she said. “I always have. That doesn’t make me weak.”

Agatha frowned, stepping in front of her. “I know,” she said, softly, wiping the tears from her face with another paper towel. Rio’s eyes widened slightly at the touch. “I’m not judging you, even though you judged my Hawaiian pizza.”

“That’s different,” Rio defended weakly. “It’s from Canada.”

Agatha snorted. “So I should be mocked for having Canadian pizza then?”

“Anybody should,” Rio muttered. Agatha barked out a laugh, shaking her head.

“You are ridiculous,” she said, rolling her eyes affectionately. 

Rio pouted and sniffled, and Agatha fought the urge to lean in and catch her bottom lip with her own. Instead, she started to move back away, but Rio’s hand on her hip stilled her. Agatha flushed, her eyes widening at the warm touch, once again, at her lower back. 

Rio’s big brown (very watery) eyes were on her now. Staring into Agatha’s own blue eyes. Agatha felt rooted to the spot, as though she wouldn’t have been able to move even if she wanted to. She swallowed thickly as Rio tilted her head. 

“Why did you leave last night?” Rio asked, which took Agatha off-guard.

“What?” Agatha asked, blinking down at her. “Because my car was double-parked, remember? I didn’t want to get a ticket.”

“But you kissed me,” Rio said, and Agatha’s stomach fluttered. Something in her had thought (prayed? Dreaded?) Rio would be the one to bring it up, but she didn’t think it would happen so soon. She’d thought that maybe they’d have a little more time to ignore it.

“Right,” Agatha said, breaking eye contact as her face burned. “Yeah, I did. I’m really sorry about that. I shouldn’t have–”

“Left.”

“Huh?” Agatha asked, her eyes flicking back up to meet Rio’s again.

“You shouldn’t have left,” Rio clarified. “I didn’t even get a chance to reciprocate.”

Agatha’s knees felt weak. Was that from the pumpkin harvesting, the MS, or…?

She felt Rio’s fingers squeeze her hip a little bit. Agatha swallowed thickly, her heart hammering against her ribcage as their eyes locked again.

“S-sorry,” she said, clearing her throat, “I just…I thought…I figured…” she let out a soft groan and closed her eyes. “I honestly don’t know what I thought. Your hand is very distracting.” 

The corners of Rio’s lips quirked up at that. “Oh?” she asked, rubbing her thumb against the denim of Agatha’s overalls. Agatha felt the touch as if it were burning straight to the bare skin at her hip. Her breath stuttered in her lungs, her throat was suddenly dry. Their faces were getting closer, but Agatha couldn’t tell if Rio was the one moving closer or…

“How could I have possibly been putting seeds in the ground wrong?”

Agatha took several steps back, her eyes going wide when Rio tossed the milk at her and motioned toward the fridge. Agatha nodded and shoved what was left of the milk into the refrigerator before slamming the door shut just as Lupe, Jen, and Chuché walked through the door, the two former bickering.

“If you don’t plant them correctly,” Lupe was saying, “then they won’t grow correctly. Tio’s gonna have a bunch of lopsided pumpkins!” She threw her hands up in the air dramatically.

“At least they’ll have character then,” Jen retorted, leaning against the island. “I can use them as part of an art installation.”

“You’ll have to pay for them first,” Lupe said, walking to the sink. “Don’t touch!” she scolded Jen as the woman reached for a tostada chip. “Your hands are covered in dirt and manure. That’s so gross!”

“Manure?” Jen practically squealed. “I didn’t know there was manure in that muck!” She held her hands away from her body as she rushed to the sink, hip-checking the child out of the way and pumping a generous dollop of foaming soap onto her hands.

“How do you think we get the pumpkins to grow so nice and vibrant?” Chuché said, handing Jen a hand towel before stepping up to the sink himself.

“Is it really the shit that does that?”

“Language,” Lupe said, shoving her aside to also stick her hands under the spray.

Jen rolled her eyes, but Agatha didn’t miss the fond smile on her lips as she went back to the island, grabbing a chip and immediately dipping a chip into the red bowl. Rio opened her mouth to warn her, but Agatha subtly shook her head over Jen’s shoulder. Rio pressed her lips together instead and just waited for the show to start.

Jen didn’t disappoint. Within seconds she was pacing around the room, fanning her mouth with tears streaming down her face, begging for water.

“Water isn’t going to help,” Chuché told her, munching on his own chip piled high with the red bowl guacamole. “You need milk.” He nodded toward the fridge. Agatha sent a grin toward Rio as she opened the fridge and pulled the milk back out, handing it right over to Jen, who demolished it in seconds.

It was impressive.

Well, to everybody except for Tio, who came walking down the hall just as Jen swallowed the last bit, still sweating and fanning her mouth.

“Did you just drink all my milk?” he asked, hands on his hips.

“Sorry!” Jen said, wiping her forehead. “I couldn’t help it. Too hot. I’ll buy you more.”

“Red bowl?” he asked Chuché. 

“Red bowl,” everybody responded in unison.

“Don’t worry about it,” Tio chuckled. “Consider it a thank you for all the work you’ve done today…and an apology for what’s going to happen later when that stuff gotta come back out.”

Jen groaned, pressing her hand to her stomach at the thought. Agatha snickered, shaking her head. She caught Rio’s eye from across the kitchen and found that the other woman was already smiling at her. She felt her face go warm and she swallowed thickly, looking back down at the bowls of guacamole, plucking another tostada.

 

They were driving back to Westview (Jen insistent that she had to shower thrice before her date with Alice) when her phone vibrated with a series of texts.

Rio💀🌺(4:57PM): Do you have any plans tonight?

Rio💀🌺(4:57PM): I mean, besides helping Jen get ready for her date with Alice

Rio💀🌺(4:58PM): I still have to pay you for all your help with the pumpkins.

Rio💀🌺(4:58PM): Not in pizza though

Rio💀🌺(4:59PM): But maybe a drink?

Rio💀🌺(4:59PM): Or ice cream? My mouth is still burning.

Agatha snorted at that last one while they were sitting at a light.

“What’s so funny?” Jen asked, trying to peek over at the texts. 

“Nothing,” Agatha said, turning her phone away. “Stop being nosy.”

“Is it Rio?” Jen asked in a teasing tone, throwing in a little shoulder shimmy for good measure.

“You’re a child,” Agatha huffed, putting her phone back into her pocket as the light turned green.

“I know you are, but what am I?” Jen taunted. Then she stuck out her tongue.

“What does Alice see in you?” Agatha huffed.

“Her own to–” Agatha reacted immediately, slapping her hand over Jen’s mouth.

“I hate you,” she growled. “I mean it this time.” 

She could feel Jen’s grin against the palm of her hand, felt the vibration of her snort and the little puff of air on the side of her hand. Jen swatted her hand away, gently.

“Don’t be so dramatic,” she said. “So what plans does Rio have?”

Agatha considered not telling her. She considered driving in silence for the rest of the trip, dropping Jen off and only speaking to threaten her about getting her clothes back in a timely manner (she fully expected Jen to bring up The Hoodie again). But she honestly wanted to talk to somebody about this. And Jen was pretty much her only friend.

“Drinks,” she said. “Or ice cream.”

“Why not both?” Jen asked. “Honestly, ice cream sounds pretty good right now.” She fanned at her mouth. “Damn, that guacamole was hot.”

“It was good, though,” Agatha said.

“So good,” Jen agreed. She’d taken some of the “Rio” guacamole after she stopped practically sobbing from the spicy stuff. Then she’d switched to the jalapeño guacamole, finding a happy medium there. “But damn that was a shock.”

“It was funny, too,” Agatha snorted, cackling when Jen shoved her shoulder. “You want us to crash?” she asked.

“We’re like two blocks from my apartment,” Jen said. “If we crash, I’ll just walk home.”

“I’ll make sure you get the full impact,” Agatha threatened. “Don’t test me.” 

Jen rolled her eyes. “Anyway,” she said, “are you gonna do it? Go out for drinks with Rio?”

“I’m leaning more toward the ice cream idea, actually,” Agatha said.

“Aren’t you lactose intolerant?”

“What’s your point?”

“You really wanna be gassy when things heat up with your girl?”

“I’ll take a Lactaid,” Agatha huffed. “And she’s not my girl.”

“Deny all you want, girl. You and I both know the truth.”

“I hate you.”

Jen blew her a kiss.

Agatha flipped her off.

 

An hour and a half later, she was driving toward Rio’s apartment, her stomach already twisting itself into knots – and they hadn’t even had the ice cream yet!

Agatha had texted Rio back as soon as she got through her front door, ten minutes after dropping Jen off with both middle fingers raised. Jen had blown her another kiss and laughed as she disappeared into her building. Agatha rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t fight the smile that pushed at the corners of her lips.

She’d texted Rio to ask if she knew of any good ice cream places, and Rio texted back a couple minutes later to let her know that there was a parlor around the corner from her apartment building that served handmade ice cream. They even had vegan options, she said, and it honestly tasted better than the full-dairy kind.

Agatha’s heart had fluttered at that. Had she ever mentioned her lactose intolerance to Rio? If she had, she couldn’t recall. If she hadn’t, then how did Rio know? Was she just that observant? Was it only because she noticed that Agatha only took oatmilk in her coffee? Plenty of people without intolerances did that. 

Besides, Agatha still ate pizza the night before, and she was pretty sure it had real cheese.

In all honesty, cheese and most dairy products didn’t bother her as much as straight milk did. Ice cream was usually hit or miss, too. 

She still popped a Lactaid, just in case she decided to be reckless and go for one of the non-vegan options.

After setting a time and place to meet (outside Rio’s apartment, around seven), Agatha hopped in the shower and scrubbed every inch of her body practically raw. She was absolutely covered in dirt and muck and (apparently) manure. She used the expensive oils and soaps she typically saved for special occasions, dousing herself in more than she normally would have used, until she smelled like vanilla and cedarwood, inhaling the scents like a balm. She used some kind of fancy conditioner Jen had gotten her that was supposed to ‘enhance’ her curls. It had been sitting under Agatha’s sink for the better part of the last year, but she finally cracked it open, wondering if it would add some kind of shine or volume to her hair.

She shaved. 

Not a lot. No woman would ever make her go bare – she was not a preadolescent girl – but she trimmed and neatened and spent far too long trying to make everything symmetrical. Her fingers were pruny by the time she stepped out of the shower and she only had about half an hour to change into fresh clothes and dry her hair (which would definitely not get dry in that amount of time). It was still slightly damp as she slipped into a pair of jeans and a soft, light brown sweater with an embroidered leave pattern that shifted colors, from yellow to red to a darker brown. Underneath, she wore a simple red tee in case she got too warm.

It was still unseasonably warm for mid-October. 

She slipped into her converse and grabbed a beanie to cover her drying hair (so as not to catch a cold) and slipped out of the house with her wallet and phone in her pocket and her keys hanging off one belt loop on a carabiner.

Rio answered the door before Agatha could even knock twice as though she’d been standing there the entire time. Agatha wanted to tease her about it, but she’d probably have done the same thing if the roles were reversed.

How had the best part of her life become seeing a woman that she’d known for so little time?

“Hey,” Rio said, her cheeks slightly flushed as she gave Agatha a lopsided grin.

“Hey,” Agatha replied, matching her smile. She felt those butterflies spreading all over her body now. They filled her with a tingling warmth. She felt like a teenager again, crushing on some girl in her PE class.

Pathetic.

But she couldn’t seem to care when Rio’s gap was on full display, her cheeks adorably pink, her dark hair sticking out of a dark green slouchy beanie. She was wearing an orange sweater with the words “Pumpkin Spice and Everything Nice” stitched across it in swoopy handwriting and a pair of dark wash skinny jeans. Her green converse complimented Agatha’s (thank you, color theory) and were just as well-worn.

She smelled like Irish Spring, obviously having just taken a shower.

Agatha caught herself staring and blinked her eyes, clearing her throat as she refocused her attention…on Rio’s sweater.

“I didn’t take you for a pumpkin spice kinda girl,” Agatha said, motioning at the sweater. It was funny and cute. It definitely matched Rio’s usual humorous taste in clothing.

“Oh,” Rio said, glancing down as if remembering what she’d put on, “I’m not. This is Dulce’s. I figured she wouldn’t mind if I borrowed it for the night. It feels fitting for today, don’t you think?”

Agatha had to agree. 

“So,” she asked as Rio stepped out of the apartment, turning to lock the door, “where is this ice cream place?”

“Around the corner,” Rio replied, “like I said. You’re gonna love it. It’s been around for ages, since well before Dulce and I moved in here. We actually went there for dinner the day we officially moved in.”

“They serve other things besides ice cream?” Agatha asked.

“Nope!” Rio replied with a grin, finally turning fully to Agatha as she clipped her carabiner onto her jeans. “A little ice cream for dinner never hurt anybody though.”

Once again, Agatha had to agree. After all, that’s what she was having for dinner tonight, wasn’t she?

“Ready to go?” she asked, mainly out of formality, turning in the direction of the exit to the building.

“Just one more thing,” Rio said. 

Agatha was about to ask what else she needed (she’d just locked her apartment door, after all) when she felt a hand grasp her elbow and tug her back around, spinning on her heel and nearly falling over. Thankfully, Rio caught her.

With both her hands…and her lips.

Agatha barely registered the hand cupping her cheek or the other arm binding around her waist as the heat spread from where Rio’s lips brushed hers – gently at first, then more firmly as she began to respond, a moan slipping from her lips involuntarily as her hands came to rest on Rio’s hips. Agatha leaned in closer, her fingers clutching at Rio’s sweater, tugging her body more closely as their lips continued to brush, electricity generating between them.

But then it was over.

Rio pulled back, stumbling a bit against her apartment door as she swallowed thickly and breathed heavily. She reached for her cane, which she had placed against the doorknob, and pressed her opposite hand to her kiss-swollen lips, shuddering out a breath and giving Agatha a shaky smile.

“Now I’m ready,” she said, making her way toward the door. 

Agatha just stared at her for a long moment, in stunned silence. 

Rio made it all the way to the automatic doors and paused, looking back over her shoulder. Agatha must have looked completely stunned because Rio grinned at her, lifting her brows like she wasn’t just as wrecked by that kiss.

“You coming?” she asked.

Agatha nodded, face flushing as she rushed to catch up. Rio didn’t move; she just waited patiently until Agatha was at her side. Then she reached out, nudging Agatha’s fingers with her own.

Agatha wasted no time in accepting Rio’s hand, linking their fingers between them with a shy smile as they walked through the automatic doors together, meeting the chill of the evening with the warmth of each other’s hands. 

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 13: Swirl

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Rio go on their ice cream date. Things heat up a little bit. More Agatha lore!

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Thirteen

There were 23 flavors to choose from at Wicked Licks. 

Agatha chose two: cotton candy and strawberry mango swirl. The latter was on top on her cone, beneath a mountain of marshmallow sauce and a cherry.

“You have strange taste, you know that?” Rio teased as she hobbled in front of Agatha, leading her out into the plaza just outside the ice cream parlor, where there were benches and picnic tables. 

There were already families and teens enjoying their own Sunday evening treats beneath strings of fairy lights. There was a gazebo in the center of it all, where a bunch of teen girls were draped over the railings and each other, mostly on their cell phones as they chatted idly. Some had boba tea and others had milkshakes or orders of fries from a nearby burger joint. Rio recognized a letterman jacket from the local high school on a girl with impossibly long, gangly legs sitting next to a bubbly redheaded girl who was telling some story gesturing wildly with her boba cup. 

The jock girl was mooning at her, running her hand through her short, dark hair.

Rio just grinned at them as she and Agatha sat down on a bench.

“I prefer eclectic,” Agatha said, taking a lick of her ice cream. “It sounds way better.” There was a spot of marshmallow on her upper lip. “Besides, all you got was chocolate.” She motioned toward the cup of ice cream in Rio’s hand, which had one scoop of chocolate peanut butter and one of rocky road. They were both drowned in hot fudge and chocolate sprinkles.

Rio looked down at her ice cream and shrugged, scooping a little bit of each on her spoon. “I like chocolate,” she said, taking a bite. “Besides,” she continued with her mouth full of ice cream, “they’re different flavors. One has peanut butter mixed in and the other has almonds and marshmallow.” She swallowed. “Different.”

“It’s all chocolate,” Agatha said. “And it’s giving you a mustache.” She handed Rio a napkin with a smirk.

“I don’t need that,” Rio said, waving it off. She swiped her tongue over her upper lip, tasting the chocolate that must have smeared there when she took a bite of her ice cream. She flattened her tongue against her upper lip, trying to get as much of the chocolate as possible in one attempt. “Did I get it?” she asked Agatha.

“Um…” Agatha said, her cheeks a little pink and her blue eyes a little wide. “Not really,” she said. “I actually think you might have made the problem worse. Here, let me.”

Agatha reached out again, holding the napkin. Rio swallowed thickly, but she didn’t pull back when Agatha swiped the napkin across her upper lip, her brows furrowing in concentration as she wiped away the chocolate from Rio’s mouth. Rio was pretty sure her face was beet red and prayed that the dim lights of the courtyard didn’t out her in that regard. Agatha’s hand was warm, even beneath the napkin, and smelled like something flowery – probably some kind of hand lotion she was wearing, or perfume.

Rio liked it.

When Agatha finally pulled back, she balled up the dirty napkin and tossed it into a nearby trash can.

“Better now?” Rio asked.

“Much,” Agatha confirmed. “There’s still a line of chocolate at the corners of your lips, but there’s nothing to be done about it now. Besides, you’ll probably have a chocolate goatee by the time you’re done with your ice cream, anyway.”

“That could be cool,” Rio said. “I could look like an evil mastermind.” She gave her best impression of an evil laugh, and Agatha just rolled her eyes, but her smile was fond.

“You’re such a goof,” she said, licking her own ice cream.

“Consequence of the trade, I’m afraid,” Rio said, taking another spoonful of her ice cream. “Hey,” she said, mouth half full, “look at that: I’m a poet, and I didn’t even know I was rhyming those words.” She gave Agatha a wide grin, but Agatha just squinted at her, a half-smile on her face. “That was a Brooklyn Nine-Nine reference, by the way.”

“Never seen it,” Agatha said.

“What? Seriously?!” Rio tutted, shaking her head. “You’re zero for two on the brilliant sitcom front! Tell me you’ve at least seen The Good Place.”

Agatha just blinked at her.

“Okay,” Rio said. “Fourth date idea: vegging on my couch, bingeing as many episodes of various sitcoms as we can finish in a roughly…twelve-hour period.” 

“Fourth date?” Agatha asked, tilting her head curiously. “Pray tell, what were the first three dates?”

“Seriously?” Rio snorted. “You don’t know?”

Agatha shook her head, but there was a ghost of a smile on her lips that she tried to cover up with more licks from her ice cream, which was starting to melt even with the late Autumn chill in the air.

“Well, the first date,” Rio said, “was obviously the coffee shop and museum the other day. That’s the very definition of a cute date, especially for lesbians.”

“Okay, fair,” Agatha said, holding up her thumb as she took another lick of her ice cream. “What was the second date?”

“Last night?” Rio said, like it was obvious. “The show, the drinks, that god-awful culinary crime? Definitely a date.”

Agatha took another slow, thoughtful, lick of her ice cream (and Rio pretended that she wasn’t fighting not to stare at the slow drag of her tongue) and nodded, holding up her pointer finger. “Accepted,” she said. “And the third?”

“Uh…right now?” Rio said, snorting. “Unless…is this not a date?”

Agatha shrugged, blushing. “You invited me,” she reminded her. “Did you mean for this to be a date?”

“Well…yeah,” Rio said, looking down at her ice cream. It was becoming chocolate soup from the warmth of her hand around the cup. She stirred it a little bit with her spoon. “I mean, if you want it to be.”

She felt fingers under her chin, pushing it up until she was face to face with Agatha again. Agatha was smiling, her face closer now. “Then,” she said, her voice low as she stared Rio in the eye, “it’s a date.” 

Rio swallowed thickly and felt herself lean in. When Agatha didn’t pull back, Rio kept going until their lips were almost brushing. Then she stopped, searching Agatha’s eyes, waiting for her to close the gap. She had been the one to initiate the last kiss after all; it was Agatha’s turn to initiate the next one.

And she did.

This kiss was soft and tentative, but no less electric than their last kiss had been. Agatha’s lips were a warm contrast to the chill in the air. They tasted like her strawberry mango ice cream, sweet and fruity. The marshmallow also made them a little sticky, but Rio didn’t mind one bit. She used her free hand to cradle the back of Agatha’s head, catching some of her hair, tangling her fingers in the soft curls. Agatha’s hand stayed under Rio’s chin, holding her in place (though it was not needed) as they kissed. 

When the need for air became more pressing than the need for Agatha’s lips to stay firmly pressed to her own, Rio pulled away, inhaling the cool air through her nose in a frankly dramatic inhale. 

“Whoa,” she said, panting as she leaned back on the bench’s armrest.

“Agreed,” Agatha replied, chuckling as she leaned back, pushing her hair behind her ear. She was smiling shyly as she looked down at her lap, holding onto her ice cream, which was now…lopsided?

Rio narrowed her eyes at the ice cream cone, then looked down at her (sister’s) sweater. “Shit!” she exclaimed, staring at the big pink and orange glob of ice cream that was now staining the front of it. “Shit!” She reached for one of Agatha’s napkins and started trying to clean the ice cream off. Agatha watched her with wide eyes.

“Dulce is gonna kill me,” Rio groaned when she’d done all she could do to remove the stain (aka not much at all). 

“You could tell her I did it,” Agatha suggested. “Then she might not be so mad.”

“You know, I would be insulted by the notion,” Rio retorted, “if that wasn’t so accurate. Thanks.”

Agatha snorted, taking another lick of her ice cream. 

They ate their ice cream in silence for a while, trading shy glances and smiles. Their knees were brushing now as their bodies tilted toward each other. Rio felt warmth and electricity every time their joints brushed. She swallowed thickly, the chocolate and peanut butter making her tongue feel like it was sticking to the roof of her mouth, but she was certain that that was just the nerves. 

She glanced across the courtyard to where the teens were still scattered around the gazebo. The redhead was now wearing the brunette’s letterman jacket, leaving the latter in just a gray henley under a blue plaid flannel. She was sharing sips of her milkshake with the redhead, who offered sips of her boba in return. They kept blushing every time they shared a look longer than a second.

Adorable, Rio thought. She hadn’t had many girlfriends in high school. She was basically raising her own kid at the time, so that wasn’t too odd. But there were girls who didn’t mind having a little kid tag along on walks or to the diner for their dates. Nothing serious ever came out of those dates, but at least they were nice to Dulce, for the most part.

She’d barely even been out in high school. Well, she wasn’t wearing any pride pins, anyway. It was more of an open secret and never something that she’d denied. She’d always reacted more positively to girls hitting on her than guys. She’d preen when girls gave her compliments and show off her skills on the court when girls she’d liked were watching. If any guys expressed interest in her, she glared at them or made disgusted faces until they went away.

Immature? Sure, but she didn’t want to give any guy false hope.

And she didn’t want any interested girl getting the wrong idea.

Chapter 14: Huevos a la Mexicana

Chapter Summary

Agatha wakes in an unfamiliar place with a very familiar body on top of hers. She's not mad about it.

But things quickly so south.

Chapter Notes

The chapter title is a reference to a dish that my dad makes. It's the only way I really like to eat eggs now, it's so good. The plantains referenced in the chapter itself is something a friend of mine said to do and while I don't enjoy plantains much, I encourage you to try it because she is a culinary genius.

Enjoy the fluff and subsequent angst!

See the end of the chapter for more notes
