“What a little thief,” Agatha snorted.

“Who’s a thief?” Dulce asked, coming out of her room just next to the kitchen. 

“Agatha’s stealing your oat milk,” Rio said, pointing her spatula at the other woman as Agatha gasped.

“Rio!” she huffed. “I’m sorry, Dulce,” she said, turning to the younger woman. “I was just–”

“Don’t worry about it,” Dulce snorted. “There’s plenty more where that came from and at least somebody is using it. Rio won’t even put it in her hot chocolate.”

“I don’t like it,” Rio moaned. “It tastes…oat-y.”

“You’re a child,” Dulce snorted.

“You literally have the babiest of baby faces,” Rio shot back, pushing the eggs around in the pan.

Dulce stuck out her tongue. Rio mirrored her.

Agatha watched them, sipping her coffee. Fascinating. She’d never had a sister, but this was her exact relationship with Jen, almost. 

Rio finished the eggs and scooped them onto a plate while also heating up a flat pan and placing a couple of tortillas onto it. While they warmed, she hobbled back over to Agatha, wrapping her arms around her and pressing her face into the crook of her neck. Agatha found herself smiling softly as she took another sip of her coffee and wrapped her arm around Rio’s waist.

“No more marks,” Agatha said when she felt Rio’s lips brush against her pulse point.

“That’s not what you said last night,” Rio snickered. Agatha pinched her ass. “Hey! Not in front of the baby.”

“I’m a college graduate!” Dulce groaned, pouring herself a cup of coffee. “And gross, you two. Get a room.” She poured some oat milk into her mug and used a spoon to stir it.

“We tried that,” Rio shot back. “Last night.”

“Oh my God!” Dulce exclaimed, running straight back to her room and slamming the door shut while Rio cackled.

“You are a menace,” Agatha murmured against the rim of her coffee mug, but she couldn’t suppress her grin as she took a sip. Rio continued to nuzzle against her neck. “I’m serious: no more marks. Jen’s never going to let me hear the end of it.”

“She and Alice are practically on their way down the aisle already,” Rio retorted, scraping her teeth over one of the hickeys. Agatha gasped, her hand clenching on Rio’s sweater. She tried not to choke on her coffee as she lightly shoved Rio away. Rio gave her an exaggerated pout.

“Go check on your tortillas,” Agatha murmured, pushing her back toward the stove.

“Oh shit,” Rio said, stumbling toward the tortillas as though she’d forgotten about them entirely. She quickly flipped them, breathing a sigh of relief when the other side was only slightly black. She gave Agatha a thumbs up. Agatha snorted.

“Can you bring the plate of eggs to the table for me?” Rio asked, turning the tortillas in a circle on the pan before reaching into a nearby drawer and pulling out a colorful towel. 

“Sure,” Agatha said, picking up the plate with the still-steaming eggs and bringing it to the tiny table in the corner, along with her coffee. “What’s with the tortillas?”

“You’ve never had a breakfast burrito before?” Rio asked, tossing the first two tortillas into the towel before tossing two more onto the pan.

“I have,” Agatha said. “Usually the frozen kind, from the grocery store.”

Rio let out a dramatic gasp. “You poor thing,” she said. 

“I’ve had real ones, too,” Agatha huffed. “From delis. Usually contained bacon, as well.”

“Well, we don’t have bacon,” Rio said. “I made the last of it the other day. I need to go grocery shopping, actually.” She reached for another drawer and pulled out a pen, writing ‘BACON’ in big letters on a notepad attached to the fridge. “But the huevos a la mexicana should suffice.”

“But you’re puerto rican,” Agatha pointed out.

“I didn’t name the eggs,” Rio snorted. “Though Dulce likes to add bits of plantain and call it ‘huevos a la puertorriqueña’ because she’s a big nerd.” She flipped the tortillas. “It’s a pretty basic dish, but it’s tasty. And it tastes really good on a tortilla.”

She turned off the burner and plucked the tortillas off, wrapping them in the towels. Then she moved stiffly toward the table, using the counter to stabilize herself.

“Should you be walking around without your cane?” Agatha asked after she tamped down the urge to get up and help her. Rio was disabled, but she was still a grown woman capable of asking for help when she needed it, she reminded herself. 

“Lilia encourages it,” Rio said, nodding. “Especially when I’m in a familiar place with plenty of furniture to use as support.”

“Lilia?” Agatha asked.

“Dr. Calderu,” Rio clarified, sitting down.

“Right,” Agatha said. “I forgot she had a first name, too.”

Rio laughed at that, opening the towel and offering Agatha a tortilla. Agatha took the flat disc of bread and frowned. 

“How do I do this?” she asked Rio.

“Hmm?” Rio asked, looking down at the tortilla in Agatha’s hand and… “Shit. Sorry. The forks.” She started to get up, but Agatha put her hand up to stop her.

“I’ll get them,” she said. “Where are they?”

“Drawer next to the sink,” Rio said. “Thanks.” 

It took all of ten seconds for Agatha to locate the forks and bring them back to the table, handing one to Rio, who immediately started shoveling eggs into her tortilla. Agatha mimicked her, giving herself a generous helping of the eggs and folding the tortilla around them just as Rio did.

Somewhat.

While Rio’s burrito looked perfectly tucked and neat, Agatha’s had a tear with egg and peppers spilling out of it.

She shrugged. It was all going to the same place anyway, she thought as she took a big bite, humming at the flavor. It wasn’t spicy at all, but it wasn’t lacking in flavor. The peppers and onions had been cooked well, and the eggs were only just slightly runny, which Agatha liked.

“This is good,” Agatha said when she had swallowed most of it.

“Told you,” Rio said, grinning around her own bite of food. She finished chewing and swallowed, clearing her throat. “So,” she said, “what are your plans for the rest of the day?”

“Well, it’s Monday,” Agatha said. “So I have to go into the gallery for a bit. Then we have the group tonight.” She took another bite of her burrito.

“Right,” Rio said. “Um, about that…do you wanna…I mean, are we…” She pressed her lips together as her cheeks turned pink. She took another small nibble at her own burrito, looking pensive.

Agatha tilted her head in confusion as she chased her food with another sip of coffee. She swallowed. “Are you okay?” she asked. She’d never seen Rio look so flustered over…what, exactly? Nothing had really happened to make her this way, had it?

“I’m fine,” Rio insisted. “I just…are we going to tell the others?”

“About what?” 

The words were out of her mouth before she even realized what she’d said. She watched Rio’s face fall and her shoulders droop. Her eyes dropped back down to the burrito in her hands. Agatha’s own eyes widened with realization and she opened her mouth to take back the words, to try to explain, but Rio shook her head.

“Right,” she said. “Nothing. It’s nothing.” She took another bite of her burrito, chewing silently. “Forget I said anything,” she said, the words slightly garbled through a mouthful of food.

“Rio,” Agatha said, desperate to fix this situation, “I–”

“No,” Rio said, giving Agatha an obviously forced smile, “it’s okay. I get it. It’s fine.” She cleared her throat. “It was fun, though.”

“Yes,” Agatha agreed. “Very fun. And I–”

“You don’t have to say anything, Agatha,” Rio insisted. “I get it. It’s fine.”

Rio looked closed off, like she wasn’t about to let Agatha get another word in, stubborn and obstinate and whatever other synonyms that she couldn’t think of right at the moment as she kept eating her burrito. Then she made another one and ate that, too, while Agatha continued to hold her own, suddenly not hungry anymore. She didn’t want her coffee, either, all the food seeming to turn in her stomach.

She placed her half-eaten burrito down on the half-empty plate of eggs and pushed herself away from the table. “I think I should go,” she said, her voice quiet and defeated.

“Yeah,” Rio said, still looking down at her food. 

“I had a nice time last night, Rio,” Agatha said, trying to inject infection into her voice, praying that Rio would hear it. 

The other woman still didn’t look up. “Me too,” she said. 

She said nothing else.

Agatha sighed and padded back into the living room, locating her shoes, phone, and the beanie that Rio had knocked off her head at some point the night before, her fingers clenching around the hat as she remembered the feeling of Rio’s nails scratching her scalp, of her fingers running through her hair. She sighed and felt the burning in her nose and the corners of her eyes. She placed the hat back on her head and leaned down to give each cat a scritch behind the ears before she made her way to the door, not even bothering to call out a farewell as she left, her stomach churning.

If she hadn’t just eaten, she may have run all the way home immediately.

But her stupid car was there, parked on the street in front of Rio’s building.

There was a ticket on the windshield.

“Fucking perfect,” Agatha huffed, plucking it from beneath the windshield wipers and making her way to the driver’s side door. She got in, started the car, and immediately placed her forehead down on the wheel, making the horn beep shortly. Not that she cared.

 

“Where’s Agatha?” 

Rio paused in scrubbing the dish in her hands, but only for a second.

“She left,” she told her sister. “I saved you some eggs. They’re in the microwave.”

“Why’d she leave without you?” Dulce asked, opening the microwave and pulling out a plate made with two egg burritos. 

“Why not?” Rio asked, trying to sound casual

Obviously she wasn’t very convincing by the way her sister paused with the plate in her hands and the microwave door still open, her brows furrowed as she stared her down. Rio tried not to blink, but Dulce’s eyes were piercing. She had to look away.

“Jesus,” Rio huffed. “Don’t your eyes ever dry out?” She reached for a dish towel, drying the dish in her hand before placing it on the drying rack. 

“Nope,” Dulce chirped. “Now spill: why did Agatha leave?”

“It’s none of your business, nosy,” Rio huffed, drying her hands on the front of her jeans and limping into the living room to grab her cane – and get away from her probing sister.

She heard Dulce place the plate down somewhere and follow on Rio’s heels. She could have easily beat Rio to the living room with two legs that still held full sensation, but she let Rio stay ahead of her before she stepped in her way, hands on hips, still standing a full half-foot shorter than her big sister. Dulce gave her that stubborn look that Rio hated – mainly because it reminded her of their mother. Her nose was wrinkled, her lips were pursed, and there was a little line between her eyes that looked like Pi with the crinkle of her brows. Rio used to tease her about it being the reason she was such a smarty-pants.

Unfortunately, it only came out when Dulce was frustrated about something.

Rio still found it adorable.

She reached out to poke the little line, but Dulce smacked her hand away.

“Rio,” she said, her voice hard as stone, “what happened?”

Rio swallowed thickly, feeling a lump begin to form. She clenched her teeth for a second and sniffed before she answered: “I don’t know.”

“Bullshit,” Dulce said.

“It’s not bullshit.”

Dulce’s stare hardened; Rio actually winced.

“You look like Dad,” she said. It was something that Dulce always hated to hear, but while that look was mostly their mother, the eyes were an echo of their father’s when he disapproved of something – when he bothered to show any emotion at all, that is.

“Rio,” Dulce said, seriously, “please just tell me what happened. You two were happy, like, an hour ago. You were practically dry-humping over eggs. How do you go from that to…” she motioned to Rio, “this.”

“First of all, rude,” Rio huffed, feigning hurt. She took a deep breath. “Secondly…I really don’t know. I just…I don’t think she feels the same.”

“What?” Dulce huffed, disbelievingly. “What makes you say that?”

Rio shrugged, placing her cane back against the wall and lowering herself to the couch. “When I asked her if we were going to tell our support group about us, she kind of acted like there wasn’t anything to tell. She was really casual about it, too.” Rio looked at her feet.

Dulce perched herself on the coffee table. “What did she say exactly? What did you say exactly?”

“I asked if we were going to tell the others,” Rio said, “and then she said ‘about what?’ like last night…and the night before meant absolutely nothing.”

“I think you’re reading a little too much into this,” Dulce said. “I mean, that doesn’t sound super serious. Besides, how long have you even been dating? A week?”

“We met a week ago,” Rio said. “Technically, we didn’t even go on our first date until, uh, Wednesday?”

“Bitch,” Dulce scoffed. “I know lesbians get real serious real fast, but you expect her to already be head over heels for you in less than a week?”

“No!” Rio defended. “I just…I dunno, Duls! I’ve never been in a relationship before! Not like this! I’ve never felt for anybody what I feel for Agatha. I liked her from the first moment I saw her, you know? I thought she might feel the same way.”

“She probably does, dipshit,” Dulce said. “But her asking a clarifying question is not enough of a reason to doubt her feelings for you. Notice how she didn’t even deny that she was your girlfriend last night when I called her that?”

“She probably didn’t even hear you,” Rio said, looking away, but she knew Dulce had a point. Dammit. She hated when her baby sister was right and she was wrong. That wasn’t how the world was supposed to work.

“Oh, she definitely heard me,” Dulce retorted, smirking. “Her ears turned pink. She avoided looking at you. She pressed her lips together. She was a little embarrassed.”

“Because she doesn’t want to be my–”

Dulce hit her over the head with a pillow. “No, you dumbass,” Dulce said. “Just the opposite. I think she liked being called your girlfriend. Otherwise, she probably would have denied it herself or run for the hills. Agatha Harkness does not seem, to me, the kind of person who would stay somewhere she doesn’t want to be, with somebody she doesn’t want to be with, you know? And she stayed to do…whatever it was you two were doing last night.” Rio opened her mouth, but Dulce held her hand up to stop her words. “Don’t say anything. I don’t wanna know. All I can be sure of is that all your clothes stayed on, and I don’t want to think any further about it. Okay?” Rio nodded. Dulce lowered her hand. “Agatha likes you,” she said. “Like, she really likes you. You just need to get your head out of your ass and see that. Don’t just rush to conclusions because you’re scared about being liked by a badass boss babe.”

“You’re still obsessed with her, aren’t you?” Rio teased. 

“And trying real hard to make her my sister-in-law,” Dulce confirmed. “Don’t fuck this up for me.” 

Rio rolled her eyes, but she knew Dulce was right (though her motivations were questionable): she had let her insecurities win and probably just fucked everything up with a woman she really liked because…why? Because she was scared? Because she’d never been in a relationship like this before?

She’d had relationships before. She’d been with women before. Hot women. Gorgeous women. Women who liked her back and thought she was just as hot as she thought them. Women who stuck around for a few months, even.

But only a few months. Never longer than six consecutive. Definitely longer than a week, though.

But she’d never felt this giddy about a woman before. She’d never felt the tightness in her stomach and chest like she did when she saw – or even just thought about – Agatha Harkness. She’d never wanted to call somebody her girlfriend so much that it made her physically ache in such a short amount of time. 

And she wanted to call Agatha her girlfriend. She wanted to look at her and think, confidently, There’s my girlfriend. She didn’t want to doubt that Agatha felt the same way about her, that Rio was more than just a hookup and a few fun dates.

But she couldn’t make herself get over it – not just yet. Because, honestly, she didn’t know how Agatha felt. She was kind of too scared to even find out at this point. That’s probably why she hadn’t let Agatha keep talking earlier.

No. That was definitely why she hadn’t let Agatha keep talking earlier. Because if Agatha didn’t verbally reject her, like Rio was fearing, then Rio was the one who was putting an end to…whatever this was before it could really take off.

And that was better.

Wasn’t it?

“Earth to Rio.” Dulce waved her hand in front of her sister’s face. Rio blinked and swallowed thickly. “You good, dude?” 

“I’m fine,” Rio said, rubbing her eyes. “Sorry. I just…I fucked up, I think.”

“Duh,” Dulce huffed. “I know I’m the smart one, but you’re not dumb, ya know. You might be blind, though.” She held up her hand. “How many fingers am I holding up?”

She flipped Rio off, and Rio slapped her hand away, glaring at her.

“Asshole,” she muttered.

“You raised me,” Dulce pointed out with a shrug.

Rio rolled her eyes and decided not to comment on that. It wasn’t because she had nothing to say. It wasn’t.

“How do I unfuck it up?” she asked. “How do I make amends?”

“Just…talk to her?” Dulce shrugged. “I dunno, dude. I have a similar situation to work out with Morgan, or did you forget?”

“Well, in your case, you’re just trying to let somebody down easy who has a crush on you,” Rio pointed out. “In my case, I’m–”

“Professing your undying love for the bossest bitch in Westview?”

“Chill out,” Rio said, her face beginning to flame with embarrassment. “Like you said, it’s been about a week.”

“That’s at least six months in lesbian time,” Dulce retorted.

“As if you would know.”

“I know a little more about that kind of thing than you think,” Dulce said, her own cheeks turning a little pink.

“What does that mean?” Rio asked, her eyes widening slightly. “Are you…?”

Dulce shrugged. “No clue still,” she admitted. “I’ve liked guys in the past. I had a whole-ass boyfriend even.”

“Whom I still plan to murder,” Rio interjected.

“Good luck with that,” Dulce snorted. “And I’ve definitely found women hot in the past. And present.”

“Like Agatha?” Rio asked.

“Ew, no, that’s my future sister-in-law,” Dulce said, wrinkling her nose. “Gross.”

Rio rolled her eyes.

“I was thinking more…Yelena? Maybe?”

“Dulce, she’s like two years older than me!”

“And insanely hot. Have you seen her arms?” Dulce pretended to wave herself. “Also, that Peggy chick can also get it.”

“I’m buying you a chastity belt,” Rio muttered. 

“God forbid a girl has fantasies about hot women!” Dulce huffed. “Anyway, the point is that I do find women attractive, and I’d like to explore that. The trick is letting Morgan know that I’m into women, but I’m just not…”

“Into her?” Dulce nodded, blushing. Rio reached out and squeezed her knee. “It’s not going to be easy,” she said, “and she probably won’t be the most mature about it, being nineteen and all, but…I think that eventually she’ll get over it. She’ll find another cute queer girl to be her girlfriend, probably at college, and forget she ever saw you as anything more than a friend. Just give it time.”

Dulce nodded, frowning. “I just hope I haven’t lost her as a friend completely, you know? Morgan’s younger, yeah, but she’s probably the best friend I’ve ever had.”

“Hey!” Rio said, taking back her hand as if burned.

“You know what I mean,” Dulce grumbled. “The best friend I’ve ever had that wasn’t forced to raise me. It’s a plus that Morgan hasn’t changed my diapers, trust me.”

“But then how will she ever really know you?” Rio teased, patting her knee. “Ponder that.” 

Dulce made a face as Rio stood, grabbing her cane. “Where are you going?” she asked as Rio began to hobble toward her bedroom.

“I’m going to take a shower, get changed, and head to the gallery to possibly beg for forgiveness,” Rio answered.

“Possibly?” Dulce called out after her as she approached her bedroom down the hall.

“We’ll see how it goes,” Rio replied, over her shoulder. “I might need to get on my knees for other reasons.” She grinned when Dulce started gagging.

Her smile dropped when she shut the door behind her, though, and she swallowed thickly, feeling her chest and stomach grow tight.

But not in the good way. Not at all in the good way.

Chapter 15: MS Hug

Chapter Summary

Agatha is stressed out and it's affecting her body -- and art -- in ways that are really only adding to the stress.

Rio has come to the conclusion that she is, in fact, an idiot, but it doesn't hurt to get a second opinion.

Chapter Notes

I am going to try to come up with a regular schedule for this fic, but I will not abandon it, I swear. I am taking part in the Big Bang so I am in the process of outlining that story right now, as well as working two jobs. This economy, amiright?

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Fifteen

Agatha sat in front of her easel, pencil in hand, determined to finish the sketch and get started on painting the sun…rise? Set? 

She still didn’t know, but she wasn’t going to get anywhere if she couldn’t figure out how to style the figure’s hair. She’d put it off for too long already. And there was no time like the present to get it done.

Especially when she could use this painting as a distraction from…way too many other things. She sighed and placed her pencil against the paper just above the woman’s head, sketching a long line that stretched from the center of the woman’s head all the way down to her waist, where the dress shirt Agatha had sketched for her spilled out of a pair of wide-leg trousers. 

Agatha drew a second line. 

And then a third. 

And then more lines. And more until she had the loose outline of a full head of long, wavy hair cascading over the woman’s shoulders. The woman’s pale eye continued to stare back at Agatha as she attempted to add some sort of shape to the hair, feeling frustrated with the way the strands wouldn’t fall quite right over her face as she attempted not to ruin what she’d already made.

She felt like Pygmalion, attempting to make a perfect work of art only to be frustrated by her own inadequacies. She took a deep breath and placed her pencil down, pushing away from the easel and standing up. She stretched her back, feeling a few pops in her spine as she grunted in relief, rubbing the sore spots. 

She’d been hunched over the canvas for at least the last hour, just based on how stiff her back was and the shift in the sun from her window. She had meant to go straight to the gallery after changing at home, but she found herself lacking the motivation to leave her house at the moment. 

She tried not to think of the reason why as she stretched her legs and ignored the photograph on her wall on her way out the door. She padded toward the kitchen in her bare feet and made her way to the kitchen, grabbing a water bottle from the fridge. Her stomach growled lightly as she took a long sip from the bottle, but she didn’t really feel like eating anything, as hungry as she apparently was.

She really wished she had finished that burrito, or at least that she had taken it with her. It was stupid to have left it there. Stupid to let food go to waste. She was certain that Rio had tossed it the second Agatha walked out the door. She probably never wanted to see Agatha again.

The plastic bottle crinkled in her hand as Agatha’s grip tightened around it and she screwed the cap back on, practically slamming it onto the counter, her eyes burning and lower lip trembling. 

“About what?”

“Stupid,” she whispered to herself. “So fucking stupid.”

“About what?” 

She ran her hands through her hair, her fingers tangling slightly in the knots. 

“About what?”

There was a lump in her throat and tightness in her chest as she struggled to breathe. It felt like somebody was squeezing her from behind, but not the way Rio had earlier.

“About what?”

Agatha spun around, but there was nobody there. She was alone. She was always alone. She made sure of it, either on purpose or…

“About what?”

Agatha covered her ears and shook her head, backing herself up against the island and sliding down to the tiled floor. She could still feel that tightness in her chest, squeezing her from the inside out. She closed her eyes tight and started humming to drown out the words that played on repeat in her head.

It didn’t work.

“About what?”

Agatha pulled out her phone and swiped through her contacts, landing on a name and pressing it. She put the phone on speaker and listened to it ring.

Once. Twice.

“Hello?”

“Dr. Calderu?” Agatha choked out. She honestly hadn’t expected the doctor to answer her own phone. Usually she got a receptionist or assistant first. She’d only called the doctor two or three times to be fair, though. She sniffled and tried to steady herself and her voice. The pain in her chest didn’t lessen at all. “It’s Agatha Harkness.” She didn’t wait for the doctor to respond. “Can MS cause a heart attack?”

“It can,” Dr. Calderu responded, evenly (re: way too calmly), “in extreme cases. Moreso, it can cause inflammation that leads to heart disease. It’s unlikely to happen in your case since it’s so early in the progression. What, exactly, are you feeling?”

“Tightness,” Agatha said. “In my chest. Around my entire abdomen actually. Like there’s a snake coiling around my body.”

“Ah,” Dr. Calderu said. “The MS hug.”

“The fucking what?!” Agatha demanded. “This doesn’t feel like a hug.”

It did, actually, but an unwanted one.

“It’s just what we call it,” Dr. Calderu explained, calmly. “It can be caused by dysesthesia, or lesions in the spinal cord. Or, simply, from stress or heat. You’re a runner, yes?”

“Yes,” Agatha confirmed, “but I didn’t run today.”

“No? Why is that?” Dr. Calderu asked.

“I…”

I woke up underneath another one of your patients and then implied that we were just having fun and I had no interest in pursuing anything more than something casual with her. Accidentally, of course.

“I felt I needed to prioritize my art today,” Agatha lied. “I haven’t really been doing much of it lately.”

“Why do you think that is?” 

“What is this, twenty questions?” Agatha huffed. “I don’t have to explain myself to you. Just please tell me how to get rid of this stupid hug thing.”

“It should go away on its own,” the doctor informed her, calmly. “It’s usually caused by stress or heat. Is there anything causing you particular stress?”

“No.”

Yes.

“Do you have a fever?”

Agatha felt her forehead.

“No,” she said. Her forehead felt pretty cool, from what she could tell. She didn’t have a thermometer. But she didn’t feel hot at all. If anything, she was kind of cool. Her toes were bare on the tile. Maybe she should put on socks.

“Did you sleep well?”

Images of Rio’s smiling face above hers flashed in Agatha’s mind. The feeling of her lips on Agatha’s lips, on her throat, her collarbone…

She can’t even remember falling asleep the night before, but she hadn’t meant to stay over. She had just not wanted to leave when Rio made her feel so…

“Could lack of sleep really cause this?” She rubbed her sternum. It ached. She took a deep breath. That ached, too.

“Yes, it’s a possibility. Usually chronic insomnia can lead to the Hug. Have you had trouble sleeping over the last few days or weeks? I could prescribe something to help you sleep. A mild sedative.”

“No,” Agatha said. “It’s fine. I just…it’s not that big a deal.”

There wasn’t as much pain as there was discomfort. She pushed herself to her feet with her phone cradled between her head and her shoulder.

“Maybe it is just stress,” she said. “I mean, we have another showcase at the gallery this weekend, so…” She shrugged and the phone nearly fell to the ground before she caught and fumbled with it a moment. “Maybe that’s it.”

“Could be,” Dr. Calderu agreed. “Just let me know if there’s anything I can do to help.” She cleared her throat. “How is it going with your medication?”

“Ugh,” Agatha said, looking toward her fridge. “Don’t remind me.”

“You’ve been taking it as you should?” Dr. Calderu sounded like her grandmother now: slightly chastising.

“I missed a dose yesterday,” Agatha confessed. “But I’ll take it today. I just…I hate needles.”

“I understand,” the doctor said, “but this is important. So that the disease does not progress too quickly, you must keep up with your injections.”

“I know,” Agatha sighed. “I will. It’s not that bad, really. I just…I hate that stupid lump under the skin. It itches.”

“Massage the spot while you ice it,” Dr. Calderu advised. “It should help.”

“Thanks,” Agatha said.

“And the group?” Dr. Calderu said. “Have you gone?”

“Twice,” Agatha said. 

“And do you like it?” She could hear the smile in Dr. Calderu’s voice.

Agatha thought of Rio.

“A lot,” she said, honestly. “I might have to miss tonight’s, though, since I have to work on setting up for the showcase.”

That was a lie. The showcase was Jen’s responsibility this week, not Agatha’s.

“It will still be there on Thursday,” Dr. Calderu said. “I even show up from time to time to see my patients. Keep going with it; the women there are all lovely.”

“Yeah,” Agatha agreed, still thinking of Rio. “They are.”

 

Rio’s grip tightened on the handle of her cane as she hobbled into the gallery. Her leg was tingling from walking so long without a break, but she didn’t want to give herself enough time to change her mind and hobble back to her apartment to hide away in shame. 

Dulce would absolutely murder her if she did.

“Miss Vidal!” the young woman working the front counter exclaimed, smiling that big, bright smile of hers. “Welcome back! Here to look at some more artwork?”

“Actually,” Rio said, “I’m here to see Agatha.”

“Agatha?” The girl furrowed her brow and pursed her lips. “Miss Harkness hasn’t come in today. Not yet, anyway.”

“She hasn’t?” Rio asked. 

Agatha had mentioned there being another showcase happening at the gallery the upcoming weekend. Jen would be handling all the logistics, but Agatha would probably still be expected to help out in any way that she could. She had been certain that Agatha would come straight to the gallery to help out after leaving Rio’s.

“Nope!” the young woman said. “She doesn’t come in every day, though. Sometimes she works from home. Sometimes she comes in a little later.” She looked at her watch. “Not this late, though.” It was already past two. “I guess you’ll have to catch her another time.”

Rio nodded, her heart sinking. “Sure,” she said, trying and failing to give America a forced smile. “Another time. Thanks.”

She started to turn away, but then another idea occurred to her. “Is Jen here?” she asked.

“Miss Kale?” America chirped. “Yes, she is!” She motioned toward the offices to the side. Agatha’s door was closed with the lights off, but the adjacent door – presumably Jen’s office – was cracked open, and the lights were clearly on. “She’s a little busy with preparations for our upcoming showcase, though, so she might not–”

Rio was already hobbling toward the office, starting to sweat a little from the effort not to collapse as her leg went almost completely numb. She didn’t even bother to knock on Jen’s door, instead simply letting herself inside and dragging herself to the nearest seat – which just so happened to be a hot pink easy chair that Rio practically disappeared into the second she sat down.

She still breathed a sigh of relief as she started to massage her leg, flexing her foot and stretching out her calf, trying to get the feeling back in the nerve-damaged limb. 

“Uh…hello?” 

“Hey,” Rio responded, still massaging her leg as she looked up at Jen, who was sitting in front of a pile of paperwork on her desk, her pen poised over an open folder. “I hope I didn’t disrupt anything important.”

“Um…” Jen said, looking between Rio and the folder in her hand. She closed the folder. “Not really, I guess. Can I help you with something?”

“Have you seen Agatha?” Rio asked. Might as well get right to it.

“Not today,” Jen said, picking up her phone. “I don’t have any texts from her, anyway. Why? Is she not answering your calls and texts? Did you guys have a sucky date or something?”

“No!” Rio huffed. “Why would you even…our date was fine! Better than fine, actually.”

Her cheeks flushed when she thought of the previous night, of lips kissing and hands roaming and bodies pressing together. Sure, they’d kept all their clothes on, but Agatha’s legs had still wrapped around Rio’s–

“Hello?!” Jen huffed. “You gonna sit there blushing, or are you going to explain why you’ve come to me to ask about Agatha when you could just, I dunno, text her?”

“Uh…”

Jen’s eyes narrowed immediately at that.

“What did you do?” she demanded.

Rio was taken aback by the steel in Jen’s gaze. They didn’t know each other well, so she hadn’t exactly expected this reaction from the taller woman. And she was just noticing how much taller – and likely in better physical shape – Jen was than her.

“Why do you assume I did something?” Rio asked, defensively. It was hard to be defensive when she was absolutely sinking into this frou frou pink, fuzzy couch though. She tried to push herself up, but her hands just sunk into the cushions as well.

“Because you’re the one who’s come looking for her,” Jen pointed out. 

It was sound logic, Rio had to admit. And it wasn’t too far off from the truth. Rio had been the one to fuck shit up. She’d let her insecurities get ahead of her and shut down over a stupid question.

“About what?”

She closed her eyes against the memory of those words. They were such simple words. Reasonable words, really. Agatha had obviously just been asking for clarification and Rio had just…panicked. Like a spooked horse.

She hated horses. 

“What, was the sex bad or something?” Jen snorted, crossing her arms over her chest and cocking her hip. “I didn’t take you for a bad lay.”

“What?!” Rio exclaimed, face flaming. “No! We didn’t even– that’s none of your business, Jennifer!”

“Ugh, the full name,” Jen huffed, wrinkling her nose. “I hate that.” She took a deep breath and leaned back against her desk. “So what was it then? What did you say?”

“Again, why do you assume –”

“Which one of you is in my office right now?” Jen asked, raising one eyebrow.

“Only because I can’t get out of this stupid couch,” Rio grunted. “I’m about to slip between these absurdly fluffy cushions. Are you a prepubescent girl or something?!” 

“Stop dodging the question,” Jen said, pushing off from the desk and sauntering over to offer her hand to Rio. Rio glared at the perfectly manicured fingers.

“When was the last time you saw Alice?” she asked.

Jen rolled her eyes. “I’ve washed my hands since then, don’t worry,” she said. “You won’t catch any of Alice’s cooties.”

“What about yours?” Rio snarked.

“Look, if you’d rather slip between the cushions…”

Rio huffed and reached for Jen’s hand, allowing herself to be tugged to her feet. Jen was surprisingly strong and sturdy for someone so thin. And her hands were almost annoyingly soft and unblemished for somebody who supposedly worked so much with chemicals to create her own paints. 

“You need help to a chair?” Jen asked, her voice a little softer now as she stepped back, still close enough to offer Rio a hand if she needed it.

“My legs still work, somewhat,” Rio said, grabbing her cane and hobbling toward one of the chairs in front of Jen’s desk. “Thanks.”

“Anytime,” Jen said. It sounded genuine.

The chair Rio sat in was just as pink as the couch but much sturdier. The cushion barely budged under her weight, which was a relief.

“So,” Jen said, sitting down in her own seat across the desk from Rio, “what happened?”

“It’s none of your business,” Rio groused.

“Then what are you still doing here?” Jen looked tired as she leaned back in her seat, manicured nails tapping on the arms of her expensive-looking leather chair. It, too, had a kind of rose tint. Everything in this woman’s life seemed to be pink. “You can leave at any time, you know. I don’t think Agatha’s coming in today, anyway.”

“She’s not?” Rio’s entire body seemed to deflate at that. 

“You see, it’s reactions like that that make me think something did happen,” Jen said, pointing at her, “and you do need my help to fix it. So spill: what happened between you and Agatha?”

“We didn’t have sex,” Rio said, defensively.

“Yeah, you’ve already said that,” Jen replied. “I know that part. I asked what did happen.”

“We slept together.”

“But you just–”

“Literally slept, Jen,” Rio clarified. “Like she–well, we both slept on my couch last night after…making out a little.”

Jen’s eyebrows shot straight up and nearly left her head. “How much is a little?” she asked, her voice cracking. There was an unmistakable smile threatening the corners of her mouth, but Rio could see her physically fighting to stay casual about it. Her eyes shone with joy, however.

Fucking weirdo.

“An hour or so, I dunno,” Rio huffed. “Don’t tell Agatha I told you that, though. Something tells me she doesn’t really want anybody to know about it.”

Jen’s brow furrowed at that. “What would make you say that?” she asked. 

Rio shrugged. “I dunno,” she said, looking down at her lap. “It didn’t seem like she was really all that into it.”

“After making out with you for an hour, it didn’t seem like she was into it?” Jen snorted and shook her head, her eyes wide with disbelief as she stared at Rio. “After falling asleep with you on your couch, it didn’t seem like she was into it? Girl, is your brain okay?”

“I mean, there are definitely a few lesions I could do without,” Rio said, scratching her head through her beanie with a shrug.

“You might have a few new ones affecting your judgement because what the actual fuck?” Jen snorted. “Do women often make out with you when they’re not into it? Is that just a popular passtime that I’m unaware of? A way to fight off the boredom?”

“Fuck off,” Rio muttered, feeling her face heat up. Jen was making too many good points. She didn’t like it. “I just…I asked her if she wanted to tell our support group about us tonight and she…didn’t seem into it.”

“So?” Jen asked.

“You sound like my sister!” Rio huffed. “This is a big deal, isn’t it? I mean, we’ve had, like, three dates already. She was kissing me just this morning! Is that not a thing!?”

“Girl, be so fucking for real,” Jen said. “I know Agatha, and relationships are a big deal to her. You don’t get to decide whether she is in one just because you made out for a little bit one night. Besides, what, exactly, did she even say that’s making you act this dumb about it?”

Rio pressed her lips together for a long moment, her arms crossed over her chest, before taking a deep breath and telling Jen everything that had happened, starting with the kiss over ice cream the night before (“Oh my god, that’s adorable!”) and ending with Agatha walking out halfway through breakfast.

She spared no detail, reasoning that Agatha probably would have told her the entire thing eventually, anyway. Besides, it felt good to get it all off her chest to somebody who probably wouldn’t hit her over the head with a pillow.

“You’re an idiot.”

Well, at least she didn’t have a pillow right at this very moment.

“To be fair, you’re both idiots,” Jen added. “But you even moreso because what do you mean you tried to DTR and then just shut down over two words?”

“What’s DTR?” Rio asked, tilting her head.

“Define the Relationship,” Jen said, snapping her fingers. “Keep up, dummy.”

“Fuck off,” Rio huffed, but she couldn’t deny that Jen was a little bit correct. Rio had already admitted it to herself and her sister.

Still, Jen had no right to–

“Agatha likes you,” Jen said. “It’s so blatantly obvious that she likes you. The fact that you’re the only one who can’t seem to see it even with her tongue down your throat is so pathetic that it’s almost impressive. You’re like the poster child for useless lesbians everywhere.”

“Do you often roast your so-called sister’s crushes like this or am I just a special case?” Rio deadpanned after a long moment of letting Jen’s words sink in.

“You’re the dumbest case I’ve seen in half a decade, that’s for sure,” Jen said, leaning her chin on her hand. “What are you so scared of?”

“What?” Rio asked. “I’m not–”

“Yes, you are,” Jen said, not letting her finish. “You’re terrified. That much is clear.”

“Did Dulce call you?” Rio asked, narrowing her eyes.

“I might have gotten a text that says, and I quote, ‘My sister is a dumbass.’” Jen shrugged. “I had no idea what she was talking about until right now, though. And I have to say that I definitely agree with her on that.”

“I’m gonna dropkick that kid out a window when I get home,” Rio muttered to herself. “Look, I just need to know where Agatha is so that I can apologize to her and try to work this out. Do you think you can help me with that?”

“I can try,” Jen said, noncommittally. “But Agatha is a stubborn bitch. She doesn’t always listen to me about shit even when she should. Also, I have no idea where she is. She was supposed to come in today to sign some papers for our showcase, but she texted me that she was staying home and would sign the papers tomorrow if I really needed them.”

“So she’s probably at home then,” Rio concluded. 

“Or she went for a run,” Jen pointed out. “That’s what she does when she’s stressed out.”

Rio’s face fell. “Do you think I stressed her out?” she asked.

“Not you, specifically,” Jen assured her. “Just…the situation.” She shrugged. “Maybe a little bit you, as well.”

Rio breathed out a little puff of air. “Any chance you’d give me her address?”

“Nope,” Jen said. “Agatha would quite literally kill me if I did that. You’re just gonna have to stalk her at work like a normal person.”

“You have a very skewed outlook of what ‘normal’ is, you know that?”

“So I’ve been told,” Jen said. “You think she’ll show up at your little group thing tonight?”

“I doubt it,” Rio said. “She hasn’t answered any of my texts, so she’s probably avoiding me.”

“Are they still going through?” Jen asked.

Rio checked her phone. All of her texts were marked ‘delivered’ but none of them had been marked ‘Read’ yet.

That could mean nothing if Agatha just turned off the read receipts though.

“They’re still going through,” Rio informed her.

“Then she hasn’t blocked you yet,” Jen pointed out. “That’s a good sign. She blocked me immediately after–” She clamped her lips shut, her eyes widening.

Rio’s eyes shot to her face, gaze narrowing. “After what?” she asked.

Jen swallowed thickly, shaking her head. “Nothing,” she said. “Nothing.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed further, channelling her inner-Dulce as she fought to keep herself from blinking. She leaned closer, not saying anything, and she could swear a bead of sweat formed on Jen’s forehead as she leaned back in her chair.

“After,” she said, feeling herself starting to lose the battle to keep her eyes from blinking, “what?”

Jen swallowed thickly. She opened her mouth, about to say something that looked as though it pained her. But then, before a single sound could escape her lips, her phone began to vibrate on her desk and she breathed out a sigh of relief.

“Sorry,” she said. “I have to take this. I trust you can make your own way out. Thanks!” She hastily picked up the phone and turned the chair so that she was facing away from Rio. “Hey, Mom!” she said into the receiver.

Rio let out a breath from her nose in frustration, but she didn’t argue. She just stood, leaning heavily on her cane, and hobbled toward the door.

“Do you want this open or closed?” she asked, over her shoulder.

“Oh, you can just leave it open,” Jen said, chipperly, waving at Rio.

Rio nodded, stepping out into the foyer, and slammed the door shut behind her, giving Jen the finger through the little window before she made her way toward the exit.

Chapter End Notes

The MS Hug is a real thing and it SUCKS btw.

Afterword

End Notes

I was diagnosed with Multiple Sclerosis when I was 29 years old, just two months shy of my thirtieth birthday. My diagnosis story is exactly the same as I wrote for Agatha in this chapter. I didn't think anything was going to be wrong and then it was. I grappled with the fact that I have MS for a long time. It's not as devastating as I originally had thought it was (due in large part to the public conversations surrounding it and the celebrities who come out about having it, who are further along than I am in the progression of their disease), but it's still something that I have to live with every single day.

But I'm living, so...

Anyway. I hope you enjoy this story. I do intend to make major edits at the end of it and possibly publish it with all original characters, so I hope that you can give me all your thoughts and feelings in the comments. Thanks!

Please drop by the Archive and comment to let the creator know if you enjoyed their work!
